that NFTs will be displayed in virtual and physical reality.</li>\n<li>The billionaire investor is bullish on crypto assets and NFTs.</li>\n<li aria-level=\"1\"><strong><a href=\"https://newsletter.businessinsider.com/join/4np/10-things-opening-bell?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestce=markets&#38;utm_medium=ingest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Sign up here for our daily newsletter, 10 Things Before the Opening Bell</a>.</strong></li>\n</ul><p>Mike Novogratz said that NFTs could be worn like jewellery one day thanks to augmented and virtual reality.</p><p>The billionaire investor gave <a href=\"https://open.spotify.com/episode/5jFlp0lOmHwceLJoC2DoH7?si=df6171c2bd8347ec\">insight into his thoughts</a> on how NFTs will be displayed in the future on his podcast Next with Novo following a conversation he had with Urs Fischer, a Swiss visual artist in a previous episode. Fischer released his first NFT artwork, a combination of an egg with a BIC lighter, earlier this week. It will be on sale from Sunday.  </p><p> &#34;I thought, what about that egg floating over my shoulder as I&#39;m walking down the street&#34;, Novogratz said on his podcast. &#34;It&#39;s the only one of its kind and just like people wear jewellery, maybe I&#39;ll wear that egg&#34;, he continued. </p><p>Passersby would be able to see it through their augmented reality glasses. Wearing NFTs as jewellery would allow people to show off their unique digital assets in the form of earrings or rings for example, said Novogratz.</p><p>NFTs, or non-fungible tokens, are digital artworks that include images, videos or audio that are unique and registered on a blockchain. NFTs have surged in popularity recently, as more artists flock to the digital space and auction houses sell pieces for sky-high prices. </p><p>Auction house Christie&#39;s announced on Thursday that it would be <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/news/christies-auction-cryptopunk-nfts-larva-labs-ethereum-ether-cryptoart-2021-4-1030288724\">presenting a set of nine so-called CryptoPunks</a>, some of the first crypto artwork at an auction next month and were expecting the digital asset to sell for $7 million-$9 million. The auction house was also behind the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/art-auction-nft-beeple-top-selling-most-expensive-sale-millions-2021-3?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestgest\">sale of an NFT by Beeple</a>, which was purchased for a record-breaking $69 million. </p><p>Talks of the NFTs being in a bubble have surfaced recently. Bobby Lee, crypto exchange founder, told Insider that <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/nft-market-outlook-huge-risk-beeple-buyer-bubble-vignesh-sundaresan-2021-4-1030282090\">bubbles may be developing in some areas</a> of the market. </p><p>Novogratz, who is bullish on crypto assets generally, said he believes that NFTs will be displayed in virtual and physical reality, for example &#34;in your little digital man cave&#34; but also on screens in physical spaces.</p><p>&#34;None of us really know how far this NFT thing can go&#34;, the billionaire investor said. But he believes that the way reality is experienced will change in the coming years, as different screens and versions of reality come together and interact with each other. </p><p>&#34;NFTs are going to be much bigger than everyone thinks they&#39;re gonna be&#34;, he ended.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a is complicated. </p><p>Social-media influencers once made the bulk of their earnings from sponsored posts. Now, they turn to a variety of revenue streams to make money.</p><p>Some creators, like <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/behind-making-tiktok-star-addison-rae-brand-item-beauty-2020-8\">Addison Rae Easterling</a> or <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-uta-builds-dtc-businesses-for-influencers-like-emma-chamberlain-2020-8\">Emma Chamberlain</a>, are launching direct-to-consumer product lines. YouTuber MrBeast (Jimmy Donaldson) launched a national <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/mrbeast-burger-team-on-influencer-ghost-kitchens-and-expansion-plans-2021-2\">burger chain</a> late last year.</p><p>Other social-media stars are licensing their image and IP to toy makers, retailers, and legacy media companies.</p><p>Child star <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/inside-ryans-world-business-interview-youtube-tv-toys-2020-9\">Ryan Kaji</a> drove hundreds of millions of dollars in sales last year by turning his toy-focused YouTube channel into a suite of products sold on Walmart and Target shelves. And YouTube stars have landed content deals with streaming platforms like Netflix or legacy TV networks like the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/youtube-stars-the-try-guys-producing-food-network-special-2021-2\">Food Network</a>.</p><p>Creators who got their start on social media are building full-fledged media companies with <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/youtubes-rhett-and-link-how-they-built-mythical-entertainment-income-2020-1\">dozens of employees</a> tied to their personal brand. And they&#39;re hiring a wave of attorneys at legacy and newcomer law firms to protect their business interests at the negotiating table and in court.</p><p>&#34;[Content creators] have an incredible amount of leverage because they actually built their own audiences and they own their own distribution channel,&#34; said Anita K. Sharma, founding managing partner at Sharma Law, which represents internet stars like TikToker Brad Mondo and YouTube creator Joshua Weissman. &#34;We&#39;re basically general counsel for each talent, and each talent is their own business. Andrew Cuomo on a 2015 flight headed to Puerto Rico for hurricane relief.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Joe Marino/NY Daily News via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Gov. Cuomo flew in a state-owned private plane over 460 times in a 5-year span, costing taxpayers nearly $650,000.</li>\n<li>A former female aide said the governor asked her to play strip poker with him on the plane.</li>\n<li>Cuomo has denied that allegation.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>New York Gov. Andrew Cuomo frequently uses a state-owned airplane and helicopter to reach the far corners of the state for official business, costing taxpayers nearly $650,000 from 2015 through April 2020, an Insider analysis found.</p><p>Cuomo faces <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/andrew-cuomo-scandals-summary-sexual-harassment-nursing-homes-impeachment-resignation-2021-3\">multiple ongoing scandals</a> and a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/andrew-cuomo-impeachment-timeline-months-rather-than-weeks-2021-3\">months-long impeachment probe</a> spurred by allegations of sexual misconduct from <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tenth-cuomo-accuser-says-he-kissed-her-without-her-consent-2021-3\">10 women</a>.</p><p>One of the allegations against him involved the governor&#39;s official state airplane, known as King One. Former economic development aide Lindsey Boylan wrote in an essay that during a flight in November 2017, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/former-cuomo-staffer-describes-sexual-harassment-in-new-essay-2021-2\">Cuomo asked her to play strip poker</a>. Cuomo has denied that allegation, and his office disputed her claim that she was alone with the governor, a state trooper, and a press staffer.</p><p>Boylan, who is currently running for Manhattan borough president, did not return Insider&#39;s request for comment.</p><p>The governor also uses a private plane for non-governmental travel that&#39;s paid for by in-kind donations, a former aide familiar with his travel patterns and logistics told Insider.</p><p>Insider used a list of state police planes and helicopters from the New York State Trooper&#39;s website and tail wing numbers registered as New York State Police aircraft to identify the passenger aircraft model used by Cuomo.</p><p>By reviewing five years of the governor&#39;s monthly public schedules, Insider identified that Cuomo flew in this state plane over 460 times accruing some 400 hours of total flight time over 5 years.</p><p>The Cuomo administration has not yet responded to Insider in its Freedom of Information Law request for financial records detailing his air travel expenses. A Cuomo spokesperson referred Insider&#39;s list of questions to New York State Police.</p><p>Nel Stubbs, Vice President at Conklin &#38; de Decker, an aircraft market intelligence and consulting company, estimates that this plane model costs $1,616 per hour to operate, according to her company&#39;s database. This figure is calculated using estimated fuel cost, plane maintenance, landing fees, and crew incidental expenses not including salary.</p><p>Flight crew salary, insurance, or the cost to maintain the plane in its Albany hangar, however, are not included.</p><h3>&#39;It is crazy old. Terrifying to fly on it.&#39;</h3><p>The twin propeller plane used by Cuomo has had <a href=\"https://www.wsj.com/articles/after-a-few-hairy-incidents-gov-cuomo-wants-new-aircraft-1484265403\">several safety scares</a>, with the governor&#39;s office pushing in recent years for an updated fleet of aircrafts they share with New York State Police.</p><p>&#34;It&#39;s crazy old,&#34; the former aide told Insider, recalling dicey flights that left newcomers on King One thoroughly spooked. &#34;Terrifying to fly on it.&#34;</p><p>One of the helicopters had to make an <a href=\"https://www.democratandchronicle.com/story/news/politics/albany/2017/01/11/cuomos-helicopter-makes-emergency-landing/96462302/\">emergency landing in 2017</a> after the cockpit began filling with smoke, according to local news reports at the time.</p><p>As a general practice, Cuomo uses the chopper for trips downstate to New York City, Long Island, or the Hudson Valley, according to the former staffer. If an event is outside of those regions or within driving distance in the Capital Region surrounding Albany, the governor takes King One.</p><p>However, the flight records obtained by Insider show some flights as short as 15 minutes without a return trip. King One&#39;s return to the hangar from those trips were not factored into Insider&#39;s cost estimate analysis.</p><p>The time saving of air travel in a state as big as New York is significant, particularly when it comes to the far flung cities and towns across the Upstate region.</p><p>Cuomo&#39;s flights from Albany to New York City were usually around 40 to 45 minutes, while driving a motorcade into the city would take between two and a half to three hours. For a trip west to Buffalo, flying takes a little over an hour, while the one way trip by car would take at least four hours.</p><p>The governor&#39;s travel sometimes came in bursts, such as on April 21, 2020, when he flew from Albany to Buffalo, then from Buffalo to Washington D.C., and then back from the nation&#39;s capital to Albany.</p><p>If the main chopper known as Sikorsky is undergoing maintenance or repairs, an older helicopter called Bell 430 is used instead, the former aide said.</p><p>&#34;I swore never to fly on that helicopter again,&#34; Melissa DeRosa, Cuomo&#39;s top aide who has been <a href=\"https://www.wsj.com/articles/cuomo-advisers-altered-report-on-covid-19-nursing-home-deaths-11614910855\">implicated in allegedly manipulating data on COVID-19 nursing home deaths</a>, told the Wall Street Journal in 2017 when she was serving as his chief of staff. </p><p>&#34;Unfortunately, given the demanding schedule we keep, it&#39;s not really an 00:41:45","updatedTime":"2021-04-10 00:41:45","title":"Tesla just hiked the prices of its most popular cars - here's how much each model will set you back","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/tesla-cost-breakdown-buying-guide-2021-3","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60705a0630004b0019b26d80?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Tesla Lineup \" height=\"1667\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Tesla&#39;s cars range in price from around $40,000 to $150,000\n<p class=\"copyright\">Tesla</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Tesla sells four models - the Model S, 3, X, and Y - in several different trim levels.  </li>\n<li>Options for them include different interior colors, extra seats, and performance packages. </li>\n<li>Teslas range in price from roughly $40,000 to $150,000.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Tesla is known to quietly raise and lower prices seemingly at random.</p><p>In October, Tesla CEO Elon Musk <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/elon-musk-tesla-model-s-price-cut-lucid-unveils-air-2020-10\">dropped the price of the Model S sedan to $69,420</a> after rival Lucid announced its sedan would start at $69,900. And in March, the company <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tesla-price-model-s-3-y-vehicles-cars-cost-musk-2021-3\">hiked the price</a> for four of its models by up to $10,000. On Friday, it raised the cost of some Model 3 and Model Y trims by up to $1,000. </p><p>With price changes on a constant basis, it can be tough to keep track of it all. Those shopping for a new Tesla can consult this guide to understand the latest prices of the Tesla Model S, 3, X, and Y, and how the models stack up. </p><p>Although add-ons vary between models, any Tesla can be optioned with the $10,000 &#34;full self-driving&#34; driver-assistance package, which doesn&#39;t currently make Teslas fully autonomous. </p><h2><strong>Model S</strong></h2><p><strong><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5efa2638988ee352382e9834?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Tesla Model 3\" height=\"1666\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Tesla Model S.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.cars.com/american-made-index/\" target=\"_blank\">Cars.com</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></strong></p><p>Launched in 2012, the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tesla-model-s-402-mile-range-upgrade-the-best-2020-6\">Model S</a> sedan is Tesla&#39;s longest-running model. The luxury four-door got an overhaul at the top of 2021, which included an updated exterior and a controversial new steering yoke. It&#39;s the choice for EV buyers who have a little more to spend and don&#39;t want a crossover. </p><p>Here&#39;s how each Model S breaks down:</p><ul><li><strong>Long Range</strong>: For $79,990, the base Model S delivers an estimated range of 375 miles, a top speed of 155 mph, and a 0-60-mph time of 3.1 seconds. </li><li><strong>Plaid</strong>: The $119,990 Model S Plaid, whose name is a reference to the movie &#34;Space Balls,&#34; travels 350 miles on a charge, hits a top speed of 200 mph, and sprints to 60 mph in 1.99 seconds, Tesla says. Both Plaid models have three motors good for more than 1,000 horsepower. </li><li><strong>Plaid Plus</strong>: The $149,990 Plaid Plus is the most advanced Model S yet. Tesla says it will do 0-60 mph in under two seconds, has a top speed of 200 mph, and has a range of more than 520 miles. Deliveries are set to start in 2022. </li></ul><p>A paint color other than white will run you $1,500 to $2,500, 21-inch wheels cost $4,500, and a white or off-white interior costs $2,500. </p><h2>Model 3</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f89fded9e9fe40019009e2c?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Tesla Model 3 update\" height=\"653\" width=\"1142\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Tesla Model 3.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Tesla</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>With the debut of the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/why-i-decided-against-buying-a-tesla-model-3-2019-8\">Model 3</a> in 2017, Tesla made good on its promise to build a more affordable vehicle than the Model S or Model X that came before it. And since it launched, the Model 3 has proved wildly successful, becoming both Tesla&#39;s most popular model and the overall best-selling EV in the world in 2020. </p><p>The Model 3 comes in three flavors:</p><ul><li><strong>Standard Range Plus</strong>: The $38,490 base Model 3 gets an estimated range of 263 miles, a top speed of 140 mph, and a 0-60 time of 5.3 seconds. </li><li><strong>Long Range</strong>: The $47,490 Long Range model has an EPA-estimated range of 353 miles</li><li><strong>Performance</strong>: For $56,990, the sporty Model 3 Performance delivers a 315-mile range, a top speed of 162 mph, and a 0-60-mph time of 3.1 seconds. It also has a lowered suspension, better brakes, and 20-inch wheels as standard. </li></ul><p>A paint color other than white will set you back $1,000 to $2,000, 19-inch rims cost $1,500, and a white interior - as opposed to the standard black - costs a $1,000 premium. </p><p><em><strong>Read more: <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/teslas-stock-price-hit-has-nothing-to-do-with-bitcoin-2021-3?r=tl-sub\">Don&#39;t blame bitcoin for Tesla&#39;s stock slide - it&#39;s high-time faithful investors took some profits</a></strong></em></p><h2>Model X</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/604bd40f10c8760018b9306f?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Tesla Model X\" height=\"720\" width=\"1114\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Tesla Model X.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Tesla</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>The <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tesla-model-x-plaid-first-look-price-specs-range-horsepower-2021-1\">Model X</a> crossover is Tesla&#39;s second-oldest model behind the Model S. It hit the market in 2015. </p><p>There are two versions of the Model X:</p><ul><li><strong>Long Range: </strong>For $89,990, the dual-motor base Model X delivers 350 miles of estimated range and a 155-mph top speed. </li><li><strong>Plaid: </strong>The $119,990 Plaid version steps things up a notch with three motors that Tesla says put out 1,020 horsepower. Tesla says the high-performance crossover will have a 330-mile range and a 0-60-mph time of 2.5 seconds when deliveries start in May. </li></ul><p>Like on Tesla&#39;s other vehicles, a white paint job comes standard - black, silver, blue, or red will run you $1,500 to $2,500. Five seats come standard, and a six-seat or seven-seat layout costs $6,500 and $3,500, respectively.</p><p>A white or cream interior costs $2,000, while bigger rims go for $5,500.</p><h2>Model Y</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6a4a1fef332b0028c118db?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Model Y Sunset White\" height=\"1406\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Tesla Model Y.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Tesla</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Starting deliveries in early 2020, the Model Y compact crossover is Tesla&#39;s newest vehicle. It&#39;s based on the same platform as the Model 3, but has more cargo capacity, rides higher, and has a general shape more like the Model X. It&#39;s proving to be a hot seller just like its sedan sibling. </p><p>The Model Y comes in two versions:</p><ul><li><strong>Long Range: </strong>The $50,490 base vehicle has an EPA-estimated range of 326 miles, a top speed of 135 mph, and makes the sprint to 60 mph in 4.8 seconds. </li><li><strong>Performance: </strong>The sportier option costs $60,990, and although it gets a lower range of 303 miles, it makes up for it in performance upgrades. The crossover accelerates to 60 mph in 3.5 seconds, has a higher top speed, and comes with bigger wheels, better brakes, and a lowered suspension. </li></ul><p>There&#39;s also a more affordable Standard Range model that Tesla <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tesla-launches-new-model-y-standard-range-7-seat-option-2021-1\">briefly sold</a> starting in January. Elon Musk <a href=\"https://twitter.com/elonmusk/status/1363946797945679875\">said on Twitter</a> it&#39;s still available as an off-menu option. </p><p>Buyers can shell out an extra $1,000 for a tow hitch, $1,000 for a white interior, and $3,000 for third-row seating. A non-white paint job costs $1,000 to $2,000, while bigger rims command $2,000.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a store. The video game company also says the tech giant tried to lock in users to its phones, tablets and other devices by keeping some popular services, like iMessage, exclusive. </p><p>In a fact-finding document released Thursday, Epic cites Apple executives saying the company decided not to develop a version iMessage for Android phones as early as 2013 to avoid causing harm to the company.</p><p>&#34;The#1 most difficult [reason] to leave the Apple universe app is iMessage . . . iMessage amounts to serious lock-in&#34; said a former Apple employee in 2016.</p><p>To which Phil vice president of software engineering and the executive in charge of iOS, was afraid that &#34;iMessage on Android would simply serve to remove [an] obstacle to iPhone families giving their kids comment.</p><p>In its counterargument against the video-game maker, Apple said Epic breached its developer agreement and the app store guidelines when it created a direct pay option that circumvented Apple&#39;s in-app purchase. </p><p>The iPhone-maker said Epic has &#34;enjoyed the tremendous resources that Apple pours into its App Store to constantly innovate and create new opportunities for developers and experiences for customers.&#34;</p><p>The court case is set <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/lg-shutting-down-smartphone-business-samsung-apple-2021-4\">to start May 3</a>, (Natasha Dailey)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/6070535e4d3e410018b7032c?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn28@2020_6/2021/04/09/16-42-21-067_78108e3a81187bdb.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn84@2020_2/2021/04/09/16-42-21-967_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=3CPO3L0vWho:cHk9Dv_l9RQ:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn51@2020_2/2021/04/09/16-42-19-226_878f720a40a95dbf.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=3CPO3L0vWho:cHk9Dv_l9RQ:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn36@2020_6/2021/04/09/16-42-18-523_ab4b005d3963f029.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn91@2020_1/2021/04/09/16-42-19-669_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=3CPO3L0vWho:cHk9Dv_l9RQ:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn80@2020_3/2021/04/09/16-42-22-393_37e7b563744ffefa.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/3CPO3L0vWho":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn60@2020_1/2021/04/09/16-42-19-495_34b220f8203f3b62.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1617986505537},{"createdTime":"2021-04-10 00:41:45","updatedTime":"2021-04-10 00:41:45","title":"US Air Force's biggest planes need to do more than carry things in the next war, air-mobility general says","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/air-force-cargo-tanker-planes-do-more-in-next-war-2021-4","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60705c1f4d3e410018b7035f?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Air Force mobility C-5M Super Galaxy cargo airlifter\" height=\"1000\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Airmen load equipment on a C-5M Super Galaxy at Barksdale Air Force Base, Louisiana, May 10, 2019.\n<p class=\"copyright\">US Air Force/Senior Airman Cassandra Johnson</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>The US military believes a war with Russia or China will require its current platforms do more.</li>\n<li>For Air Mobility Command, that means cargo planes and tankers can&#39;t just be carting fuel and supplies.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>The prospect of war with a powerful adversary means the Air Force&#39;s cargo and tanker planes need to be able to do more than move supplies and fuel, according to Gen. Jacqueline Van Ovost, head of Air Mobility Command.</p><p>&#34;Look at the competition that we&#39;re in right now. Why wouldn&#39;t we change the calculus by doing different things, moving away from the antiquated view that [Air Mobility Command] just brings stuff ... and [stays] outside the threat ring to be a maneuver force to support inside the threat ring, because that&#39;s really where we&#39;re going,&#34; Van Ovost said at Mitchell Institute for Aerospace Studies <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=KfDGa0rCi8M\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">event</a> on March 31.</p><p>Mobility aircraft, particularly tankers, will be &#34;forward in the fight,&#34; Van Ovost added, making them well suited to be primary or backup &#34;nodes&#34; to process and relay information to other aircraft and outposts.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5e9a0fed92e8ba0c2423c0b6?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Boeing KC-46 Pegagus\" height=\"1372\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A KC-46.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>&#34;Our last experiment had a C-17 as the forward node to do crunching of data,&#34; Van Ovost said. &#34;It was on the ground, but we showed that a C-17 with a current setup of antennas could do that work, so why wouldn&#39;t we put that on all the airplanes?&#34;</p><p>The new KC-46 tanker, which is still struggling with <a href=\"https://www.defensenews.com/air/2021/03/12/the-kc-46-tankers-most-infamous-problem-isnt-the-one-that-impacts-pilots-the-most/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">other aspects</a> of its mission, will be the first to get a new pod developed as part of the Advanced Battle Management System, the Air Force&#39;s <a href=\"https://www.af.mil/About-Us/Fact-Sheets/Display/Article/2493560/advanced-battle-management-system/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">contribution</a> to a broader Pentagon effort to digitally connect military forces.</p><p>&#34;That&#39;s a pod on the airplane&#34; that can provide command and control, translating information between aircraft and processing data, and it could in the future be hooked up to other aircraft, such as the KC-135 tanker, Van Ovost added.</p><p>&#34;I absolutely believe that all the platforms need to be connected to provide the resilient and interoperable pathways not just for Air Mobility but to be able to allow F-35s and F-22s to talk, to be able to talk to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/us-air-force-says-the-valkyrie-drone-launched-another-drone-2021-4\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">the Valkyrie</a>, and to have resilient forward nodes that can process data and send out orders,&#34; Van Ovost said.</p><h2>Preparing for &#39;the next fight&#39;</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f9e096569331a0011bc6943?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Air Force C-17 palletized munition\" height=\"752\" width=\"1240\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A C-17 drops palletized munitions (simulated JASSMs) during Advanced Battle Management Onramp #2 testing.\n<p class=\"copyright\">US Air Force</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>The cargo fleet will likely also be carrying weapons for strikes and self-defense, Van Ovost said.</p><p>&#34;For us right now, we look at the [Special Operations Command] model that they&#39;re doing with the C-130s, and we think to ourselves, &#39;How can you do that with C-17s? What if you had a platform that could eject JASSMs out of the back of the airplane?&#39;&#34; Van Ovost said, referring to the Joint Air-to-Surface Standoff Missile.</p><p>Air Force Special Operations Command <a href=\"https://www.af.mil/News/Article-Display/Article/2199852/afrl-afsoc-launch-palletized-weapons-from-cargo-plane/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">tested</a> so-called palletized munitions in early 2021. In a separate test in September, a C-17 dropped a pallet of simulated JASSMs. The Air Force and private industry are <a href=\"https://news.lockheedmartin.com/2020-10-28-us-air-force-lockheed-martin-further-efforts-to-transform-airlifters-into-potent-strike-weapon-platforms\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">continuing</a> to develop the concept.</p><p>&#34;The name of the game is to, at lower costs, provide mass on target,&#34; Van Ovost said. &#34;Frankly, palletized munitions, that&#39;s quite the load if you can eject that out of the back of the airplane and get those things flying.&#34;</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/57b4b803db5ce954008b74cc?format=jpeg\" alt=\"KC-46A and C-17\" height=\"853\" width=\"1280\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A KC-46A refuels a C-17 Globemaster.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/File:Pegasus_refuels_Globemaster_%282%29.jpg\" target=\"_blank\">US Air Force</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Dropping bombs out of cargo plane, which other crews then guide to targets, would be faster than unloading weapons &#34;on a ramp somewhere&#34; to be reloaded onto bombers, Van Ovost said, adding that in a future experiment, Air Mobility Command will test its ability to command and control such munitions after dropping them.</p><p>Being forward also means closer to the enemy, and Air Mobility Command has been &#34;looking at high-value aircraft self-defense in all kinds of different ways,&#34; Van Ovost said.</p><p>The pod deployed aboard tankers and airlifters could be reconfigured to provide &#34;defensive capabilities,&#34; Van Ovost said. Those planes could also carry &#34;attritable&#34; systems - <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/future-war-losses-like-wwii-top-air-force-officer-says-2020-9\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">reusable but also expendable</a> - for the same purpose.</p><p>Central to all of that is &#34;battlespace awareness,&#34; of which most of the mobility fleet has &#34;zero&#34; right now, Van Ovost said, adding that putting aircraft on the same network would give them a common picture of incoming threats.</p><p>&#34;So now I may not need fighters immediately by our aircraft. Perhaps they can intercept it forward of the aircraft or ... we can have defensive counter-air attritables that are either on the wings that could launch out and do a headshot or simply electronic warfare in those pods so ... we can deflect the missile.&#34;</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fecdc55a644880018193e6f?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Air Force B-52 KC-135 refueling\" height=\"1336\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A US Air Force KC-135 refuels a B-52 over the Middle East, December 30, 2020.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Senior Airman Roslyn Ward</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Van Ovost cited the Defense Advanced Research Projects Agency&#39;s &#34;<a href=\"https://www.darpa.mil/program/gremlins\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Gremlins</a>&#34; as an example of an &#34;attritable&#34; that could be launched from a C-17 or C-5 against aerial threats and then be recaptured and rearmed.</p><p>Other traditional defenses are also an option. &#34;We have hardpoints on the C-17. We have hardpoints on the KC-46 - not a hard stretch to think that we could put one or two missiles on there for self-defense,&#34; Van Ovost said.</p><p>Talk of new roles for the airlift fleet has prompted questions about whether there are enough of those planes to do those tasks and conduct standard mobility operations, but &#34;the next fight&#34; likely won&#39;t have &#34;an iron build up&#34; at a major bases or drawn-out attrition warfare, Van Ovost said.</p><p>&#34;The next fight is going to be just-in-time, and I think the intensity is going to be much shorter,&#34; Van Ovost BROWN/AFP via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>European regulators are investigating whether Johnson &#38; Johnson&#39;s vaccine could cause blood clots. </li>\n<li>The investigation was opened after four cases were reported, including one fatality.</li>\n<li>J&#38;J&#39;s vaccine was authorized for European distribution last month, but hasn&#39;t been given out yet. </li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>European regulators are investigating whether Johnson &#38; Johnson&#39;s COVID-19 vaccine caused unusual blood clotting after four cases were reported in vaccine recipients, including one fatality. </p><p>The European Medicines Agency&#39;s Pharmacovigilance Risk Assessment Committee disclosed Friday that they are reviewing the vaccine after three people who received J&#38;J&#39;s vaccine in the US and another who was involved in a clinical trial developed blood clots. It&#39;s currently not clear if the vaccine caused these clots. </p><p>J&#38;J said that it was working closely with experts and regulators to assess data coming in, but that so far, they have found a small number of very rare side effects. </p><p>The investigation comes as European states prepare to add the vaccine to their roster of COVID-19 shots. J&#38;J&#39;s vaccine <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/european-medicines-agency-recommends-johnson-and-johnson-vaccine-to-eu-2021-3\">was recommended for authorization</a> by the EMA on March 11, but has not yet been distributed. </p><p>Approximately 4.9 million doses of J&#38;J&#39;s vaccine have been administered in the US, <a href=\"https://covid.cdc.gov/covid-data-tracker/#vaccinations\">according to the CDC.</a>  </p><h2>It&#39;s not the first time the link between vaccines and blood clots has been investigated</h2><p>The EMA has been closely watching reports of blood clots linked to another vaccine: <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/astrazeneca-vaccine-worth-it-despite-blood-clot-link-experts-2021-4\">AstraZeneca&#39;s two-dose immunization</a>. </p><p>The agency stated Wednesday that blood clots can be a  <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/astrazeneca-vaccine-side-effects-blood-clots-very-rare-ema-2021-4\">&#34;very rare&#34; side effect of AstraZeneca&#39;s shot</a> in people with low blood platelet levels. Approximately 169 cases of blood clots in the brain and 53 cases of blood clots in the spleen had been reported as of April 4, according to the EMA. </p><p>Cases of blood clots have also reported in patients who had <a href=\"https://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/10.1002/ajh.26132\">received Moderna and Pfizer&#39;s vaccines</a>, a J&#38;J spokesperson said in a statement. </p><p>Issues have been popping up as J&#38;J&#39;s shot has rolled out in the US.</p><p>One of the factories that produces both drug companies&#39; vaccines is in hot water after it was reported by the New York Times that 15 million doses of Johnson &#38; Johnson&#39;s vaccine had been <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/millions-johnson-and-johnson-vaccine-doses-need-contamination-check-nyt-2021-4\">cross-contaminated with AstraZeneca&#39;s vaccine</a> at a U.S. factory run by Emergent BioSolutions. None of those shots were distributed to the public. </p><p>Officials in <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/colorado-and-north-carolina-pause-distribution-of-jj-vaccine-2021-4\">Colorado and North Carolina</a> stopped giving out J&#38;J&#39;s vaccine this week after two dozen people experienced minor adverse reactions like nausea and dizziness.</p><p>J&#38;J&#39;s stock traded down about in coffee shop\" height=\"1414\" width=\"2121\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>WhatsApp has several security tools for protecting your data on and off the app.\n<p class=\"copyright\">d3sign/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>To improve your WhatsApp account&#39;s data security, you can enable two-step verification, disable cloud backups, and turn on security notifications.</li>\n<li>You can also <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/whatsapp-privacy-settings\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">change how much information you share through WhatsApp&#39;s Privacy menu</a>, located in the messaging app&#39;s Settings section. </li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tech-reference\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Visit Insider&#39;s Tech Reference library for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Most people who use social media and communication apps understand that a certain level of personal data is shared with the company or companies behind them. But <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/whatsapp-forcing-users-to-share-personal-data-facebook-elon-musk-2021-1\">when a WhatsApp notification</a> signaled users would have to opt-in to a privacy policy update by February 8, 2021, it caused panic. </p><bi-shortcode id=\"related-article-module\" class=\"mceNonEditable\" data-type=\"5f46935b5af6cc2fd552ef5e\" data-title=\"What is WhatsApp? A guide to navigating the free internet-based communication platform\" data-url=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-is-whatsapp-guide\" data-thumbnail=\"https://i.insider.com/undefined\">Related Article Module: What is WhatsApp? A guide to navigating the free internet-based communication platform</bi-shortcode><p>WhatsApp&#39;s last major <a href=\"https://blog.whatsapp.com/looking-ahead-for-whats-app\">privacy policy update</a> was back in 2016 and offered users 30 days to opt-out of some metadata and user info sharing between itself and Facebook. But it wasn&#39;t until the 2021 update that many users became aware WhatsApp&#39;s parent company might have more access to their data than they realized. </p><p>In January, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/whatsapp-privacy-policy-delay-three-months-2021-1\">Insider reported</a> that WhatsApp confirmed their new policy would &#34;not expand our ability to share data with Facebook.&#34; Around a month later, due to confusion among users, the company announced it would slowly rollout the opt-in with a new deadline of May 15. And if users don&#39;t opt-in, some aspects of the app, like messaging, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/whatsapp-privacy-policy-may-15-messages-calls-2021-2\">will stop working</a>.</p><h2>WhatsApp security tips for protecting your data</h2><p>You can&#39;t stop what WhatsApp shares with Facebook now, but if you <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/whatsapp-facebook-data-terms-conditions-privacy-signal-2021-1\">aren&#39;t among those who migrated</a> to messaging apps like Signal or Telegram, here are a few additional suggestions beyond <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/whatsapp-privacy-settings\">privacy setting protections</a> for keeping your WhatsApp data and personal information safe from anyone<em>. </em></p><h2>Enable Two-Step Verification</h2><p>Two-step verification is offered by many apps and is well worth using, especially since it essentially ensures no one else can log into your app or device but you. Activating this feature in WhatsApp is relatively simple and takes only a few seconds. </p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/606f27b04d3e410018b70004?format=jpeg\" alt=\"WhatsApp data 1\" height=\"1039\" width=\"1242\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>You can enable two-step verification in your Settings.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Jennifer Still/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Here&#39;s how to enable two-step verifications in your WhatsApp settings. </p><aside class=\"breakout-box headline-regular\"><h3><strong>How to enable two-step verification on WhatsApp</strong></h3><ol><li>Open your WhatsApp Settings.</li><li>Select Account. </li><li>Choose the &#34;Two-step verification menu.&#34; </li><li>Next, tap &#34;Enable&#34; and create a six-digit passcode. You&#39;ll need to enter this periodically and whenever you register WhatsApp on a new device. </li><li>Enter an email address should you forget or lose your code.</li></ol></aside><h2>Disable automatic cloud backups</h2><p>While some people want to keep records of their conversations, doing so leaves those conversations vulnerable to prying eyes who could gain access to iCloud or Google Drive where they&#39;re stored. This is because backed-up conversations lack the encryption of live ones within WhatsApp, so it&#39;s important to disable this option. </p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/606f27e330004b0019b26a75?format=jpeg\" alt=\"WhatsApp data 2\" height=\"1930\" width=\"1242\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>WhatsApp allows iOS and Android users to backup their app data.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Jennifer Still/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><aside class=\"breakout-box headline-regular\"><h3><strong>How to disable automatic cloud backups on WhatsApp for iOS</strong></h3><ol><li>Go to your Settings. </li><li>Choose &#34;Chats.&#34; </li><li>Select &#34;Chat Backup.&#34; </li><li>Next tap &#34;Auto Backup.&#34; </li><li>Choose &#34;Off.&#34; </li></ol></aside><aside class=\"breakout-box headline-regular\"><h3><strong>How to disable automatic cloud backups on WhatsApp for Android</strong></h3><ol><li>Tap the Menu icon.</li><li>Select Settings. </li><li>Choose Chats. </li><li>Tap Chat Backup. </li><li>Select Backup to Google Drive. </li><li>Choose &#34;Never.&#34; </li></ol></aside><h2>Turn on security notifications </h2><p>You can have WhatsApp alert you if another device gains access to your private conversations by enabling security notifications. Given that WhatsApp creates a security code whenever a device joins a conversation if that code ever changes, you need to know about it. Here&#39;s how to toggle on this option. </p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/606f281730004b0019b26a76?format=jpeg\" alt=\"WhatsApp data 3\" height=\"1228\" width=\"1242\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Get updates about your contact&#39;s security settings.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Jennifer Still/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><aside class=\"breakout-box headline-regular\"><h3>How to turn on security notifications on WhatsApp</h3><ol><li>In your Settings, tap Account. </li><li>Select Security. </li><li>Tap the &#34;Show security notifications&#34; toggle and turn the lever green.</li></ol></aside><bi-shortcode id=\"related-article-module-end-of-article\" class=\"mceNonEditable\"><a data-type=\"602ecca606adf851e8357fe5\" data-title=\"How to 00:41:45","updatedTime":"2021-04-10 00:41:45","title":"Bill Hwang lost around $20 billion in 2 days when his Archegos fund imploded, report src=\"https://i.insider.com/60702e954d3e410018b702c4?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Bill Hwang\" height=\"719\" width=\"1438\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Bill Hwang&#39;s Archegos Capital Management imploded in March.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=vnbeQ-WFOUU\" target=\"_blank\">YouTube</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\"><li>Bill Hwang built a fortune of around $20 billion but lost it in a matter of days, Bloomberg reported.</li><li>His hedge fund Archegos Capital Management ballooned on successful bets on global tech firms.</li><li>But it all came crashing down when Hwang&#39;s highly leveraged bets started to go awry.</li><li id=\"recirc\"><strong><a href=\"https://newsletter.businessinsider.com/join/4np/10-things-opening-bell?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestium=ingest?utm_source=markets&#38;utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&#38;utm_medium=ingest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Sign up here for our daily newsletter, 10 Things Before the Opening Bell</a>.</strong></li></ul><p>Bill Hwang built up a fortune of around $20 billion through savvy investments, but then lost it all in 2 days in March as his Archegos investment fund imploded after some of his bets went awry, a report has said.</p><p>Hwang, an alumnus of famed hedge fund Tiger Management, took around $200 million in 2013 and turned it into a $20 billion net worth by betting successfully on technology stocks, <a href=\"https://www.bloomberg.com/news/features/2021-04-08/how-bill-hwang-of-archegos-capital-lost-20-billion-in-two-days\">Bloomberg said</a> in the most detailed look at Archegos&#39; finances yet.</p><p>But it all came crashing down at the end of March when some of Hwang&#39;s highly leveraged bets started to go wrong and his banks sold huge chunks of his investments. The sales knocked <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/stock-market-wall-street-speculating-hedge-fund-liquidation-archegos-2021-3\">around $35 billion</a> off the value of various US media and Chinese tech firms in a day.</p><p>Bloomberg reported that Hwang&#39;s early investments through his Archegos Capital Management <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/archegos-liquidation-spotlight-unregulated-family-offices-leverage-swaps-2021-4\">family office</a> included <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/amzn-stock\">Amazon</a>, travel-booking company <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/expe-stock\">Expedia</a>, LinkedIn and <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/nflx-stock\">Netflix</a>, the latter of which reaped a $1 billion payday. Bloomberg cited people familiar with Hwang&#39;s investments.</p><p>Hwang&#39;s bets at some point shifted towards a broader range of firms, in particular media conglomerates <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/viac-stock\">ViacomCBS</a> and <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/disca-stock\">Discovery</a>. He also loaded up on Chinese tech companies such as <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/bidu-stock\">Baidu</a> and <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/gsx-stock\">GSX Techedu</a>.</p><p>Archegos&#39; investments powered it to a strong final quarter of 2020, with many of the stocks it held jumping more than 30%.</p><p>But the ViacomCBS bet would become particularly problematic for Hwang. It started to tumble during the week starting March 22, causing Archegos&#39; prime brokers - the major banks who lent it money and processed its trades - to demand more money as collateral, known in the business as a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-is-a-margin-call\">margin call</a>.</p><p>With Hwang unable to put up the cash, Morgan Stanley sold around $5 billion of Archegos&#39; holdings at a discount, according to Bloomberg. Goldman then followed suit, selling billions of dollars of companies&#39; stock.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/goldman-sachs-stock-picks-for-higher-eps-earnings-growth-consensus-2021-4\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Goldman Sachs handpicks 40 stocks that will enjoy bigger earnings growth than Wall Street expects in 2021</a></em></p><p>Some banks weren&#39;t so fast, however, with Credit Suisse and Nomura left nursing estimated losses of <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/credit-suisse-posts-loss-after-archegos-blow-up-exec-departure-2021-4-1030275805\">$4.7 billion</a> and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/nomura-takes-2-billion-loss-after-last-weeks-sell-off-2021-3\">$2 billion</a> respectively.</p><p>A key reason that Hwang&#39;s wealth collapsed so spectacularly is that he used large amounts of <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/archegos-meltdown-guggenheims-millstein-says-regulators-look-leverage-prime-brokerage-business2021-4-1030278927\">leverage</a>. That is, Archegos borrowed lots of money to fund his investments, meaning it faced large losses when they went bad.</p><p>Gerard Cassidy, US bank analyst at RBC Capital Markets, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/archegos-liquidation-spotlight-unregulated-family-offices-leverage-swaps-2021-4\">told Insider</a> in March: &#34;Leverage is always a two-edged sword. In a bull market when prices are rising it enhances your returns. And then in a falling market, like you just saw in this particular case, it cuts your head off.&#34;</p><p>Archegos was unavailable for comment but spokesperson Karen Kessler told Reuters at the end of March: &#34;This is a challenging time for the family office of Archegos Capital Management, our partners and employees.&#34;</p><p>&#34;All plans are being discussed as Mr. Hwang and the team determine the best path forward,&#34; she said.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/crypto-arbitrage-trading-strategy-alameda-research-sam-bankman-fried-billionaire-2021-4\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">A 29-year-old self-made billionaire &#34;Crazytown.&#34;</p><p>&#34;Crazytown was populated by jackasses, and media hounds, and some normal citizens as baffled as I was about how we got trapped inside the city walls,&#34; Boehner writes party movement within the Republican Party boosted Boehner to the highest-ranked position in the House in 2011, but by late 2015, Boehner resigned from the top post as the increasingly-influential conservative caucus plotted to get rid of him.</p><p>Boehner has previously <a which hits stands on Tuesday. He particularly took aim at Sen. Ted Cruz of Texas, calling him &#34;a reckless a--hole who thinks he is smarter than everyone else.&#34;</p><p>Boehner argued in his book that these fractures in the GOP eventually prompted the rise gloated about their efforts to edit scientific reports on COVID-19 last year to fit Trump&#39;s messaging, according to documents obtained by <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/health/2021/04/09/cdc-covid-political-interference/\">The Washington Post</a> on Friday.</p><p>An investigation by a congressional subcommittee on COVID-19 found that a team of Trump appointees at the Department of Health and Human Services &#34;engaged in a persistent pattern of political interference in the nation&#39;s public health response to the coronavirus pandemic,&#34; Democratic Rep. Jim Clyburn of South Carolina, the subcommittee chair, wrote to two former officials, coronavirus advisor Scott Atlas and science advisor Paul Alexander. </p><p>According to The Post, emails reviewed by the panel show that Trump officials had been &#34;overruling and bullying scientists and making harmful decisions that allowed the virus to spread more rapidly,&#34; Clyburn wrote.</p><p>In one email sent on September 9, Alexander wrote to Michael Caputo, the then-assistant secretary for public affairs at HHS, touting a &#34;small victory but a victory nonetheless and yippee!!!&#34; about an alleged change to the first line of a CDC report on virus transmission among young people.</p><p>In another email sent on September 11, Alexander asked Atlas to help him &#34;craft an op-ed&#34; that would challenge an upcoming CDC report about COVID-19 deaths among young patients.</p><p>&#34;Let us advise the President and get permission to preempt this please for it will run for the weekend so we need to blunt the edge as it is misleading,&#34; Alexander wrote to Atlas, The Post said.</p><p>As the coronavirus spread across the country last spring, Trump and his allies <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-admits-downplayed-coronavirus-i-knew-it-could-be-horrible-2020-3\">frequently</a> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-told-woodward-he-always-downplayed-threat-of-covid-19-2020-9\">sought</a> to downplay the severity of the outbreak. When states pursued lockdown restrictions to combat the spread of the virus, Trump urged governors to reopen the economy, going against the recommendations of his own COVID-19 advisors. The former president and those close to him would also often neglect following public health guidelines advised by the CDC.</p><p data-el=\"text\">&#34;I know the President wants us to enumerate the economic cost of not reopening,&#34; Caputo wrote in an email to Alexander on May 16. &#34;We need solid estimates to be able to say something like: 50,000 more cancer deaths! 40,000 more heart attacks! 25,000 more suicides!&#34;</p><p data-el=\"text\">&#34;You need to take ownership of these numbers,&#34; Caputo wrote in a subsequent email to Alexander, per The Post. &#34;This is singularly important to what you and I want to achieve.&#34;</p><p data-el=\"text\">House Democrats launched an investigation into Trump appointees potentially pressuring career officials to alter the language of scientific reports after <a href=\"https://www.politico.com/news/2020/09/11/exclusive-trump-officials-interfered-with-cdc-reports-on-covid-19-412809\">Politico first reported</a> on the issue on September 11, 2020. The subcommittee has requested interviews with Alexander and Atlas as well as additional documents to complete its probe, according to The Post.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original 00:41:45","updatedTime":"2021-04-10 00:41:45","title":"4 reasons why the housing market will cool down and settle into a long and sustainable boom, Jefferies says","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/housing-market-sustainable-boom-homebuyers-mortgage-rates-millennials-construction-jefferies-2021-4","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/606f25254d3e410018b6fff1?format=jpeg\" alt=\"construction workers building home\" height=\"1000\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Construction workers build a new Centex home on Tuesday, June 23, 2020, in Houston.\n<p class=\"copyright\">David J. Phillip/AP</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>The housing market&#39;s hot streak will soon evolve to slower and more sustainable growth, Jefferies said.</li>\n<li>A historic supply shortage and massive demand sent prices soaring through 2020.</li>\n<li>Trends including a construction comeback and generational aging can fuel a steadier expansion, the firm said.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>The homebuying sprint seen throughout the pandemic will soon give way to a long and healthy jog, Jefferies analysts said Thursday.</p><p>The dramatic housing market boom of 2020 simply can&#39;t last. The surge in home sales has left mere months of supply left, and contractors are struggling to keep up. Prices leaped at <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/home-prices-climb-february-housing-market-supply-mortgage-rates-corelogic-2021-4\">the fastest rate since 2006 in February</a>, and while the pace of sales has slowed, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/existing-home-sales-february-supply-shortage-rising-prices-housing-market-2021-3\">it remains at historically elevated levels</a>.</p><p>Meanwhile, the median house price has <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/existing-home-sales-february-supply-shortage-rising-prices-housing-market-2021-3\">kept setting new records</a>, putting affordability more and more out of reach. For much of the boom, mortgage rates were falling to new lows south of 3%, but that trend has reversed in 2021, presenting another affordability challenge for prospective buyers. Jefferies expects those dynamics to rein in the rally and set the stage for sustainable and inclusive market growth.</p><p>&#34;The pandemic has been the catalyst for many buyers that were on the sidelines, pushing homeowners and renters to reevaluate their living quarters and driving the surge in demand,&#34; the team led by Philip Ng said, adding that new volatility stands to derail the market&#39;s momentum.</p><p>Here are the four trends contributing to a shakeup in the housing market&#39;s growth, according to Jefferies.</p><h2>(1) Construction will catch up</h2><p>Perhaps the biggest constraint on the housing market is its meager supply, but the supply-demand gap should spur a correction. The construction industry underbuilt for more than a decade after the housing market sparked the global financial crisis. The weak building activity led to a shortage of 2.5 million homes, but activity seen over the last year stands to change that, the team said.</p><p>&#34;The pandemic has been a catalyst for many buyers that were on the sidelines, pushing homeowners and renters to reevaluate their living quarters and driving the surge in demand,&#34; the analysts said.</p><p>The shortage now serves as &#34;an opportunity for homebuilders to pick up incremental demand,&#34; they added. Jefferies estimates another 1.8 million homes would need to be built to balance out the market.</p><h2>(2) Millennials reaching peak buying age</h2><p>Contractors will also ramp up building to match nascent demand from millennials, the firm said. Homeownership rates begin to rise with 25- to 29-year-olds and accelerate further for 30- to 34-year-olds as people get married and start families.</p><p>The population of 25- to 34-year-olds is currently 9% larger than the 35- to 44-year-old group, signaling to homebuilders that a wave of demand is on the horizon. The bank&#39;s modeling suggests monthly housing starts will land between 1.7 million and 2 million through 2024, markedly higher than the February reading of 1.4 million.</p><h2>(3) Home inflation set to cool</h2><p>Expectations for stronger inflation contributed to soaring lumber prices over the past year. Costlier building materials were estimated to be <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/real-estate-homebuying-soaring-lumber-prices-new-homes-construction-2021-3\">adding $24,000 to the cost of every new home</a>, further boosting prices amid the supply shortage.</p><p>That pressure will soon be alleviated as the economy reopens and commodity-price inflation moderates, the team said. Futures contracts suggest lumber prices will sink 26% through 2022, just as construction picks up to match robust demand, they added.</p><h2>(4) Interest rates have room to run</h2><p>Mortgage rates have <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/mortgage-rates-climb-inflation-fears-housing-market-economy-freddie-mac-2021-3\">only recently started swinging higher</a> after tumbling to record lows through 2020. The reversal stands to cool the market&#39;s buying spree as borrowing costs rise, but it won&#39;t halt purchases in their tracks, according to Jefferies.</p><p>For one, mortgage rates still sit at relatively low levels. The average 30-year fixed mortgage rate stood at 3.13% this week. Rates haven&#39;t had a cooling effect on housing-market growth since 2018 when they reached 5%. A pickup in supply could perfectly coincide with higher, but not stifling, mortgage rates, the analysts said, </p><p>&#34;With supply improving from new construction and more homes likely being listed to capitalize on elevated home prices and vaccine availability, we see home price appreciation moderating,&#34; they added.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/housing-market-sustainable-boom-homebuyers-mortgage-rates-millennials-construction-jefferies-2021-4'>Business Insider</a></div><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?a=JSv76TVUKJk:oq-PNLOyAoY:yIl2AUoC8zA\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a &#38; Johnson COVID-19 vaccine next week, after weeks of varied distribution.</p><p><a href=\"https://data.cdc.gov/Vaccinations/National-Weekly-Janssen-Allocations/2r93-e5cs\">According to the Centers for Disease Control and Prevention</a>, 4.9 million doses of the Johnson &#38; Johnson vaccine were distributed across the United States this week. Last week, about 1.9 million doses were distributed.</p><p>The slowdown in distribution comes after a plant in Baltimore mistakenly mixed up vaccine ingredients and ruined 15 million doses of the Johnson &#38; Johnson vaccine. The factory now has to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/millions-johnson-and-johnson-vaccine-doses-need-contamination-check-nyt-2021-4\">check 62 million other doses for possible contamination</a> and has yet to be <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/factory-botched-johnson-and-johnson-vaccines-distribution-certification-2021-4\">cleared to distribute by federal regulators.</a></p><p>The Dutch plant that delivered the initial supply of Johnson &#38; Johnson vaccine doses to the US also distributed doses on a varied schedule, causing a further slowdown across states, <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/live/2021/04/09/world/covid-vaccine-coronavirus-cases?type=styln-live-updates&label=coronavirus%20updates&index=0&action=click&module=Spotlight&pgtype=Homepage#johnson-johnson-vaccine-deliveries-are-about-to-take-a-big-dip-in-the-us-a-big-dip-in-the-us\">according to the New York Times.</a></p><p>As of Friday morning, at least 112 million people in the US, or 33.7% of the population, had received their first doses of the COVID-19 vaccine. More than 66 million people have been fully vaccinated, <a href=\"https://covid.cdc.gov/covid-data-tracker/#vaccinations\">CDC data shows.</a></p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article McLaughlin)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/6065c64cdaf0f10018f996ae?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn40@2020_4/2021/04/09/16-42-19-000_e291a46e8881f462.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn84@2020_2/2021/04/09/16-42-21-967_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=wOcdC2jCu_o:t4zaBRGBqMg:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn99@2020_1/2021/04/09/16-42-21-677_0d592a2b6737ab7b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=wOcdC2jCu_o:t4zaBRGBqMg:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn64@2020_4/2021/04/09/16-42-20-154_bed1436a92f7258a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn91@2020_1/2021/04/09/16-42-19-669_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=wOcdC2jCu_o:t4zaBRGBqMg:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn44@2020_4/2021/04/09/16-42-23-126_b4d1b9cf26fa3ca3.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/wOcdC2jCu_o":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn40@2020_3/2021/04/09/16-42-20-312_cecc6c362b481013.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1617986505572},{"createdTime":"2021-04-10 00:41:45","updatedTime":"2021-04-10 00:41:45","title":"I'm a CEO who allowed my remote employees to set their own working hours. We're way more productive and much happier as a result.","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-flexible-work-hours-can-improve-motivation-and-productivity-2021-4","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/607082f04943790018bb1a6c?format=jpeg\" alt=\"extra cash pandemic at home\" height=\"1129\" width=\"1506\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Having a flexible work schedule is attractive to many remote employees.\n<p class=\"copyright\">visualspace/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Jesper Schultz is the CEO and cofounder of <a href=\"https://www.basicops.com\">BasicOps,</a> a San Francisco-based task and project management system.</li>\n<li>During the pandemic, he allowed his small team to adjust their preferred working hours.</li>\n<li>Schultz says the flexibility encourages workers to prioritize their own wellness and be more motivated and productive while working.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>A year of postponed weddings, torn-up plane tickets, and far too many Zoom calls has forced us all to adapt to a new way of life. Beyond personal changes and too much time spent perfecting the art of sourdough bread baking, the workforce has also adapted. </p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/606be36fa7d803001963edff?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Jesper Schultz is the CEO and cofounder of BasicOps\" height=\"533\" width=\"711\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Jesper Schultz is the CEO and cofounder of BasicOps.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Jesper Schultz</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>For better or worse, we&#39;ve said goodbye to long commutes and water-cooler chats. A new era of remote work has taken its place, bringing far more flexibility than the traditional 9-to-5 ever gave us. </p><p>While juggling childcare and crafting an office out of your bedroom closet probably wasn&#39;t your idea of work-life balance, there are two sides to every coin, and the pandemic has forced some positive changes in the way we work, too.</p><p>Flexibility has become a necessity rather than a luxury. After permitting work schedule flexibility <a href=\"https://www.basicops.com\">BasicOps</a>, I&#39;ve seen positive shifts in our employees&#39; overall mindsets and productivity.</p><p>Here are the top five benefits of this flexibility that I&#39;ve witnessed reshaping our workplace.</p><h2>1. Flexibility leads to higher productivity</h2><p>There&#39;s a myth perpetuated by traditional office culture that our most productive hours happen between 9 a.m. and 5 p.m. This schedule may work for a portion of the population, but there&#39;s growing evidence that at least half of us operate on an altogether different productivity timeframe - and much that is calculated by our circadian rhythms.</p><p>In &#34;<a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/books/2017/sep/21/why-we-sleep-by-matthew-walker-review\">Why We Sleep</a>,&#34; sleep researcher Matthew Walker describes how up to 50% of us aren&#39;t programmed to wake up early. Our genetics determine our circadian rhythms: While you might have no trouble turning in at 10 p.m. and rising at 7 a.m., these hours may force your colleague to wake up far earlier than their natural sleeping patterns. </p><p>Losing early morning sleep has been linked to poor memory recall, trouble concentrating, poor communication, and lost productivity. Beyond the cognitive difficulties, it&#39;s also costly for companies: In a study across four large US companies, researchers found insufficient sleep costs employers almost $2,000 per employee per year. </p><p>Companies including <a href=\"https://www.yahoo.com/entertainment/nap-job-10-companies-100300632.html\">Nike and Google</a> allow employees to time their work hours to match their circadian rhythms. Employees at these companies are even encouraged to take cat naps during their workdays, with &#34;nap pods&#34; scattered throughout corporate headquarters. Other than scheduled meeting times, my employees can plan their days as they please. If they&#39;re tired after lunch and need a nap, I&#39;m totally fine with that. </p><h2>2. Remote workers take fewer sick days</h2><p>The standard workday leaves very little room for the unexpected. The 9 a.m. punch-in doesn&#39;t account for a feverish child at home or a rough night of sleep, meaning it&#39;s likely your employees will opt to call in sick. </p><p>With flexible scheduling, your employees will feel comfortable starting later to get a few extra hours of sleep or tend to a sick child at home. Rather than losing an entire day, employees can start when it suits them.</p><p>Rigid working hours lead to higher stress levels, and higher stress weakens our immune systems. One powerful way to help keep your employees healthy is by providing flexibility - that alone will decrease stress and anxiety in their daily lives. They&#39;ll take fewer sick days, and you&#39;ll likely see more motivated workers, too.</p><h2>3. Flexible schedules lead to happier employees </h2><p>If you&#39;re skeptical that a flexible schedule can improve happiness levels, look no further than Finland, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/finland-coronavirus-united-nations-worlds-happiest-country-pandemic-2020\">the happiest country in the world</a>. </p><p>Finnish workplace culture is a far cry from the American standard: For nearly 25 years, the Finns have been able to set their work hours - by law. <a href=\"https://finrepo.fi/en/news-new-working-hours-act\">The Working Hours Act</a>, put into law in 1996, allows most workers in Finland to adjust their hours as needed. With that much flexibility and control over their lives, it&#39;s not surprising that the Finns are happier than, well, everyone.</p><p>By offering a working agreement that mimics the Finns, you&#39;re allowing your employees to incorporate personal errands such as picking up the kids, attending courses, or exercise, all of which will make it far easier for your employee to juggle life and work. They&#39;ll be less stressed, more productive, and feel more balanced.</p><p>At BasicOps, all employees have the opportunity to take weekdays off and make up the time over the weekend if that works better for them. One of our employees takes hikes every Wednesday, which I think is great.</p><h2>4. Communicate more effectively with flexible work</h2><p>This may come as a surprise, but communication is far more efficient when an employee works from home or works on a flexible schedule. Between excessive coffee breaks and idle chit-chat, there&#39;s a surprising amount of time wastage in the office place.</p><p>With the pandemic has come a heavy adoption of workflow management software programs. While these programs existed pre-pandemic, the work-from-home mandates made them all the more necessary to keep projects and collaboration flowing. </p><p>Flexible and remote workers are far more likely to use these platforms to connect with colleagues than those who are in the office on a rigid schedule. By adopting such platforms, communication among teams becomes far more streamlined and efficient, saving everyone time and energy. </p><h2>5. A flexible work culture improves employee retention </h2><p>Work-life balance is the Holy Grail of today&#39;s professionals. Millennials (who now make up the largest generation in the US workforce) and Gen Z both place a high value on achieving that balance, so finding and retaining new talent will be likely more successful with flex work.</p><p>Perhaps most importantly, a flexible working agreement indicates trust and transparency between employee and employer. That not only puts employees at ease but also improves productivity. </p><p>While flexibility has been somewhat forced upon all of us during these pandemic times, it&#39;s become clear that there is a silver lining for both business and employees. The era of micromanagement is dying and flexibility must be embraced in order to keep moving forward.</p><p><em>Jesper Schultz is the CEO and cofounder of </em><a href=\"https://www.basicops.com\"><em>BasicOps,</em></a> <em>an easy-to-use internet-based platform and intuitive digital hub that enables team collaboration and communication across tasks and projects.</em></p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/how-flexible-work-hours-can-improve-motivation-and-productivity-2021-4'>Business
