the US&#39;s infrastructure problems.</li>\n<li>That influx of money would be welcome after two decades and billions of dollars squandered trying to rebuild other countries.</li>\n<li>Daniel R. DePetris is a fellow at Defense Priorities and a foreign affairs columnist at Newsweek.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>It doesn&#39;t take a genius to know that America&#39;s domestic infrastructure is in utter disarray. Travel down I-95 between New York City and Boston, and you will be lucky not to hit a 5-inch-deep pothole in the middle of the lane.</p><p>The United States, the most prosperous country in the world, <a href=\"https://www.pgpf.org/sites/default/files/0215_infrastructure_quality_ranking.pdf\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-saferedirecturl=\"https://www.google.com/url?q=https://www.pgpf.org/sites/default/files/0215_infrastructure_quality_ranking.pdf&source=gmail&ust=1617983063236000&usg=AFQjCNGTsVxVz0QkrLqObdZ1Jysx2N38EgZ1Jysx2N38Eg\">is now 13th</a> in terms of infrastructure quality, below many of its peers in Europe. <a href=\"https://www.usatoday.com/story/money/2020/08/18/states-infrastructure-roads-bridges-railroads-needing-repair/42211689/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-saferedirecturl=\"https://www.google.com/url?q=https://www.usatoday.com/story/money/2020/08/18/states-infrastructure-roads-bridges-railroads-needing-repair/42211689/&source=gmail&ust=1617983063236000&usg=AFQjCNFPv7epiLKcXZyBofN1BG3-h7HTaAN1BG3-h7HTaA\">Over 20%</a> of its roads are in poor condition. <a href=\"https://www.nbcnews.com/news/us-news/more-one-third-u-s-bridges-are-disrepair-infrastructure-group-n1183316\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-saferedirecturl=\"https://www.google.com/url?q=https://www.nbcnews.com/news/us-news/more-one-third-u-s-bridges-are-disrepair-infrastructure-group-n1183316&source=gmail&ust=1617983063236000&usg=AFQjCNFSWiEs8EBiSQcavjmz4lZlBRUApwmz4lZlBRUApw\">About 127,000 bridges</a> across the US are either structurally deficient or need to be replaced. And as the water crisis <a href=\"https://www.politico.com/news/magazine/2020/12/23/flint-water-crisis-2020-post-coronavirus-america-445459\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-saferedirecturl=\"https://www.google.com/url?q=https://www.politico.com/news/magazine/2020/12/23/flint-water-crisis-2020-post-coronavirus-america-445459&source=gmail&ust=1617983063236000&usg=AFQjCNGxcLvbLcF5WRDS3ULXOAVkLzVTgwLXOAVkLzVTgw\">in Flint, Michigan</a> showed, even clean water supplies aren&#39;t a given.</p><p>The United States, in other words, is in desperate need of investment at home. The alternative is watching as Americans who live in cities continue to suffer from dilapidated highways while their fellow citizens in rural areas are left searching for a basic broadband connection.</p><p>The juxtaposition outside US borders is stunning. Over the last two decades, as US infrastructure was worsening, Washington was busy conducting reconstruction initiatives in nations that to this day remain consumed by conflict and led by unaccountable and corrupt governments.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5980962ab50ab100028b5171?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Afganistan Iraq embassy troops soldiers\" height=\"2513\" width=\"3500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Afghan policemen stand guard outside the Iraqi embassy in Kabul after an attack, July 31, 2017.\n<p class=\"copyright\">REUTERS/Mohammad Ismail</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>As of December 2020, the US has spent approximately <a href=\"https://www.chicagotribune.com/nation-world/ct-us-afghanistan-spending-20170821-story.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-saferedirecturl=\"https://www.google.com/url?q=https://www.chicagotribune.com/nation-world/ct-us-afghanistan-spending-20170821-story.html&source=gmail&ust=1617983063236000&usg=AFQjCNEwCsdkU-j9alCsxQUOxOoop2yIOgUOxOoop2yIOg\">$143 billion</a> of taxpayer money on reconstruction projects in Afghanistan.</p><p>The projects were designed to kickstart the Afghan economy, introduce a degree of self-sufficiency over the long-term, and ensure ordinary Afghans were able to enjoy the kinds of public goods - accessible water supplies, highways, access to hospitals - that are often taken for granted in the West.</p><p>Yet the results, to put it generously, have been poor. <a href=\"https://time.com/5534783/iron-tempest-afghanistan-opium/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-saferedirecturl=\"https://www.google.com/url?q=https://time.com/5534783/iron-tempest-afghanistan-opium/&source=gmail&ust=1617983063236000&usg=AFQjCNHoKn40IJ05ABAylBsxp-SthuqRyQsxp-SthuqRyQ\">$1 billion was devoted</a> to schools in Afghanistan that weren&#39;t even operating. A $8.5 billion program to wean Afghan farmers away from growing poppy <a href=\"https://time.com/5534783/iron-tempest-afghanistan-opium/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-saferedirecturl=\"https://www.google.com/url?q=https://time.com/5534783/iron-tempest-afghanistan-opium/&source=gmail&ust=1617983063236000&usg=AFQjCNHoKn40IJ05ABAylBsxp-SthuqRyQsxp-SthuqRyQ\">was unsuccessful</a>, evident in Afghanistan&#39;s current status as the world&#39;s foremost producer of opium.</p><p>As Special Inspector General for Afghanistan Reconstruction John Sopko <a href=\"https://www.sigar.mil/pdf/testimony/SIGAR-21-25-TY.pdf\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-saferedirecturl=\"https://www.google.com/url?q=https://www.sigar.mil/pdf/testimony/SIGAR-21-25-TY.pdf&source=gmail&ust=1617983063236000&usg=AFQjCNEV3dRaEqt0V5cs8KiArn4RvCH4igiArn4RvCH4ig\">testified</a> to Congress last month, systemic corruption in Afghanistan undermines US-funded reconstruction initiatives to the point of irrelevancy. Of the $7.8 billion in US reconstruction funds SIGAR investigated, <a href=\"https://apnews.com/article/world-news-afghanistan-taliban-united-states-b07ccfc12ceb7abefab055fe7bd6cf53\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-saferedirecturl=\"https://www.google.com/url?q=https://apnews.com/article/world-news-afghanistan-taliban-united-states-b07ccfc12ceb7abefab055fe7bd6cf53&source=gmail&ust=1617983063236000&usg=AFQjCNECQDFDk5o8skmykRW8n66NosQRowW8n66NosQRow\">just $1.2 billion</a> - 15% - went to their intended purpose.</p><p>Many of the buildings paid for by the US taxpayer were left abandoned. Afghanistan still relies on international donors for 80% of its budget; remains dominated by corruption at all levels of government; and is seemingly incapable of exhibiting the slightest degree of responsibility in how it spends US taxpayer money.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/58437f2dba6eb61b008b7645?format=jpeg\" alt=\"US Soldier Selfie Iraq\" height=\"987\" width=\"1500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A US soldier takes a selfie at the US Army base in Qayyara, south of Mosul, October 25, 2016.\n<p class=\"copyright\">REUTERS/Alaa Al-Marjani</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>The US experience in Iraq isn&#39;t much better. Despite their good intentions, US officials ran into problems on the reconstruction front almost immediately.</p><p>After <a href=\"https://www.latimes.com/archives/la-xpm-2004-sep-12-fg-power12-story.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-saferedirecturl=\"https://www.google.com/url?q=https://www.latimes.com/archives/la-xpm-2004-sep-12-fg-power12-story.html&source=gmail&ust=1617983063237000&usg=AFQjCNH76RhQNJW064R7MPzYq_nFLNesqQzYq_nFLNesqQ\">an infusion of $172 million</a> to restore the Baiji power plant after the initial invasion, the plant was only churning out half of its potential output. The United States sunk billions <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/national-security/report-iraq-reconstruction-failed-to-result-in-lasting-positive-changes/2013/03/05/aa7e6948-85d9-11e2-98a3-b3db6b9ac586_story.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-saferedirecturl=\"https://www.google.com/url?q=https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/national-security/report-iraq-reconstruction-failed-to-result-in-lasting-positive-changes/2013/03/05/aa7e6948-85d9-11e2-98a3-b3db6b9ac586_story.html&source=gmail&ust=1617983063237000&usg=AFQjCNE11qY1L1ds1uwguVUMP5NJDtunOAUMP5NJDtunOA\">into large and costly projects</a> the Iraqi government was unable to handle or finance.</p><p>Schools and prisons funded by Washington were left idle, while water treatment plants in dangerous areas like Fallujah were overbudget and <a href=\"https://www.nbcnews.com/id/wbna38903955\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-saferedirecturl=\"https://www.google.com/url?q=https://www.nbcnews.com/id/wbna38903955&source=gmail&ust=1617983063237000&usg=AFQjCNHQBTlQ7-Rem67RLwE49ncmha6VWAE49ncmha6VWA\">woefully inadequate</a> for the population. Today, Iraq remains a country so riddled with parochialism and multiple power centers that Shia militias are building up <a href=\"https://www.france24.com/en/live-news/20210329-worse-than-a-jungle-the-cartel-controlling-iraqi-borders\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-saferedirecturl=\"https://www.google.com/url?q=https://www.france24.com/en/live-news/20210329-worse-than-a-jungle-the-cartel-controlling-iraqi-borders&source=gmail&ust=1617983063237000&usg=AFQjCNF6yuUVDpEb6arcamZ4mXASS1dbKwZ4mXASS1dbKw\">their own revenue streams</a> separate from the state.</p><p>As US soldiers and aid workers were essentially throwing billions of dollars <a href=\"https://www.voanews.com/usa/report-us-wasted-billions-dollars-afghan-rebuilding-projects\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-saferedirecturl=\"https://www.google.com/url?q=https://www.voanews.com/usa/report-us-wasted-billions-dollars-afghan-rebuilding-projects&source=gmail&ust=1617983063237000&usg=AFQjCNGixNdlZuQH5hllsu60eWDqjDdVgw60eWDqjDdVgw\">in the toilet</a> in Afghanistan and Iraq, America&#39;s own schools, roads, and bridges were falling apart.</p><p>Total spending on US domestic infrastructure fell <a href=\"https://www.brookings.edu/research/shifting-into-an-era-of-repair-us-infrastructure-spending-trends/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-saferedirecturl=\"https://www.google.com/url?q=https://www.brookings.edu/research/shifting-into-an-era-of-repair-us-infrastructure-spending-trends/&source=gmail&ust=1617983063237000&usg=AFQjCNHB5a8e171PIonimDtdtnorEXC0lwtdtnorEXC0lw\">between 2007-2017</a>. The American Society of Civil Engineers gave the US a &#34;C-&#34; on its infrastructure score and estimated that the US economy <a href=\"https://www.cfr.org/backgrounder/state-us-infrastructure\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-saferedirecturl=\"https://www.google.com/url?q=https://www.cfr.org/backgrounder/state-us-infrastructure&source=gmail&ust=1617983063237000&usg=AFQjCNElwtd99nLeB6MYeEY3Bn685_kRHgY3Bn685_kRHg\">could lose $10 trillion</a> in GDP by 2039 if Washington failed to plug the infrastructure spending gap.</p><p>The Biden administration, like its predecessors, is hoping to solve (or at least mitigate) America&#39;s infrastructure problems <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/us-policy/2021/03/31/biden-infrastructure-climate-plan/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-saferedirecturl=\"https://www.google.com/url?q=https://www.washingtonpost.com/us-policy/2021/03/31/biden-infrastructure-climate-plan/&source=gmail&ust=1617983063237000&usg=AFQjCNEXH508zem3wQ5yMjrCcb6Ys7DAIwrCcb6Ys7DAIw\">with an ambitious $2 trillion proposal</a> that would be paid for over a period of 15 years.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/56a6359cdd0895ad088b46af?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Flint Water Crisis\" height=\"1837\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Michigan Army National Guard soldiers hand out bottled water at a fire station in Flint, Michigan, January 17, 2016.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Bill Pugliano/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>The plan would dump $600 billion into improving and modernizing ports, railways, bridges and highways. $300 billion would be devoted to supporting domestic manufacturing, while <a href=\"https://apnews.com/article/joe-biden-technology-coronavirus-pandemic-pittsburgh-jen-psaki-8865ffc8f5ad3142155a5bd3c3a3e6d3\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-saferedirecturl=\"https://www.google.com/url?q=https://apnews.com/article/joe-biden-technology-coronavirus-pandemic-pittsburgh-jen-psaki-8865ffc8f5ad3142155a5bd3c3a3e6d3&source=gmail&ust=1617983063237000&usg=AFQjCNHRf_yV_EE0M47uLTR0nKfYtkk3ZQR0nKfYtkk3ZQ\">an additional $100 billion</a> would be invested into building up an electric grid prone to occasional outages.</p><p>Biden&#39;s initiative will run into steep opposition due to the cost. But leaving the details aside, one can&#39;t help but feel a sense of jubilation that US policymakers are actually showing some interest in investing in America rather than in countries overseas that have proven to be perpetually weak, dysfunctional, and perhaps even immune to US generosity.</p><p>Policymakers, lawmakers, and pundits still like to describe the United States as an exceptional nation in a league of its own. But no nation, not even the United States, can thrive if it underinvests in its own communities or takes its eyes of the ball to what is truly important: expanding its own strength domestically.</p><p>It&#39;s a lesson the old denizens of the Soviet Union learned the hard way - and when they finally appreciated the concept, it was too late.</p><p>America&#39;s source of power overseas is anchored in its prosperity at home. If the US is so keen on nation-building, it should start and end in its own cities and towns.</p><p><em>Daniel R. DePetris is a fellow at Defense Priorities and a foreign affairs columnist at Newsweek</em>.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a used employment projection and wage data from the Bureau of Labor Statistics. </li>\n<li>The following are the 30 best jobs of the next decade or so.</li>\n<li><a Software developers and software quality assurance analysts and testers\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60706ab6f068cf0018022bfd?format=jpeg\" alt=\"software developer programmer\" height=\"1333\" width=\"1777\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Software developers are one of the best future jobs.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Ngampol Thongsai/EyeEm/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong>Projected new positions between 2019 and 2029: </strong>316,000 &#160;</p><p><strong>Median annual earnings in 2020: </strong>$110,140</p><p><strong>Typical educational requirements:&#160;</strong>Bachelor's degree</p>\n\tMethod and data sources\n\t\n\t<p>The coronavirus pandemic has had a major effect on <a href=\"https://www.bls.gov/news.release/empsit.t17.htm\">employment</a> in nearly every industry over the past few months. However, the future of work is still looking pretty bright for medical and tech jobs, based on data and projections from the Bureau of Labor Statistics.</p><p>As Americans look forward to finding their next potential job, Insider decided to look at high-paying jobs that have bright futures ahead of them. To do this, we used two datasets available on the Bureau of Labor Statistics website.</p><p>The Bureau of Labor Statistics' <a href=\"https://www.bls.gov/emp/home.htm\">Employment Projections program</a> publishes estimates for job growth across hundreds of occupations. The <a href=\"https://www.bls.gov/emp/tables/emp-by-detailed-occupation.htm\">most recent release</a> compares how many people worked in each occupation in 2019 with the Bureau's projections for 2029. BLS notes that these estimates do not include the impact that the coronavirus pandemic has had on employment.</p><p>However, BLS published two <a href=\"https://www.bls.gov/emp/publications/pandemic-scenarios.htm\">alternate projections</a> that include the pandemic's impact to see how long-term economic impacts <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/employment-projections-pandemic-bureau-of-labor-statistics-report-2021-2\">may affect employment growth in the various occupations.</a> With any projections, the estimates may not be exactly what pans out over the next decade but can give a sense of where there may be some job growth.</p><p>We combined those job growth projections with the latest May 2020 median annual wages for each occupation from the Bureau's <a href=\"https://www.bls.gov/oes/current/oes_nat.htm\">Occupational Employment and Wage Statistics</a> program (previously called the Occupational Employment Statistics program) using the <a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geometric_mean\">geometric mean</a> of the two numbers to find roles that are both growing and high-paying.</p><p>Since we are focused on high-paying jobs, we restricted our ranking to occupations with 2020 median wages above the median among all occupations of $41,950.</p>\n</div><div 4-10 00:41:45","updatedTime":"2021-04-10 00:41:45","title":"Amazon employees in Alabama have voted against forming a union","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/amazon-union-vote-fails-bessemer-alabama-warehouse-workers-2021-4","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f05eb83f0f4192f1702770b?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Jeff Bezos\" height=\"3541\" width=\"4721\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Amazon&#39;s CEO Jeff Bezos speaks at an event in Washington.\n<p class=\"copyright\">REUTERS/Joshua Roberts</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Amazon defeated a vote to form a union at its warehouse in Bessemer, Alabama.</li>\n<li>Amazon has been aggressively campaigning against the formation of a union there since late last year.</li>\n<li>The Retail, Wholesale and Department Store Union (RWDSU) said it&#39;s officially filing objections alleging Amazon illegally interfered with the election.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Amazon workers at the company&#39;s warehouse in Bessemer, Alabama have voted against forming what would have been the company&#39;s first-ever union in the US.</p><p>The vote count finished early Friday afternoon. The final tally was 1,798 votes against unionizing and 738 votes for the union, with 505 ballots challenged and 76 ballots being voided. 70.9% of valid votes counted were against the union.</p><p>With a majority of votes against the union, Amazon has successfully defeated the unionization attempt.</p><p>Since Amazon&#39;s margin of victory was higher than the total number of challenged ballots, the challenged ballots won&#39;t be opened and the votes inside them won&#39;t be counted.</p><p>In a statement on the victory, Amazon said it was glad workers&#39; &#34;collective voices were finally heard.&#34; </p><p>&#34;It&#39;s easy to predict the union will say that Amazon won this election because we intimidated employees, but that&#39;s not true,&#34; the company said. &#34;Our employees heard far more anti-Amazon messages from the union, policymakers, and media outlets than they heard from us. And Amazon didn&#39;t win - our employees made the choice to vote against joining a union.&#34;</p><p>The Retail, Wholesale and Department Store Union (RWDSU) announced it is filing official objections with the National Labor Relations Board (NLRB) alleging that Amazon illegally interfered with the vote.</p><p>&#34;Amazon has left no stone unturned in its efforts to gaslight its own employees. We won&#39;t let Amazon&#39;s lies, deception and illegal activities go unchallenged, which is why we are formally filing charges against all of the egregious and blatantly illegal actions taken by Amazon during the union vote,&#34; RWDSU president Stuart Appelbaum said in a statement.</p><p>Unfair labor practice charges are common in contentious union elections, John Logan, a labor and employment professor at San Francisco State University who specializes in tactics companies use to defeat union drives, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/amazon-pushed-usps-to-install-mailboxes-outside-warehouse-report-2021-4\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-stringify-link=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/amazon-pushed-usps-to-install-mailboxes-outside-warehouse-report-2021-4\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\">previously told Insider</a>. He said it&#39;s &#34;fairly difficult&#34; to predict how the NLRB will ultimately rule on those charges.</p><p>Before Thursday&#39;s public vote count, both Amazon and the RWDSU also had the the opportunity to challenge employees&#39; eligibility to cast a ballot. Hundreds of ballots were challenged, mostly by Amazon, according to the RWDSU.</p><h2>A union vote that drew national attention</h2><p>The 5,800 warehouse workers had from February 8 until March 29 to cast their mail-in ballots. Amazon <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/amazon-union-alabama-workers-describe-anti-union-tactics-bessemer-2021-3\">led an aggressive anti-union campaign</a> and has fought workers&#39; efforts to organize across the country.</p><p>In Bessemer, the company papered bathroom stalls, distributed anti-union merchandise, and ran targeted advertisements encouraging workers to vote no, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/amazon-union-alabama-workers-describe-anti-union-tactics-bessemer-2021-3\">Insider previously reported</a>.</p><p>One of the RWDSU&#39;s objections centers around a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/amazon-pushed-usps-to-install-mailboxes-outside-warehouse-report-2021-4\">US Postal Service mailbox</a> that was installed outside the warehouse, in which Amazon encouraged workers to cast their ballots. According to a Freedom of Information request obtained by <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/technology/2021/04/08/amazon-bessemer-mailbox-union/\">The Washington Post</a> on Thursday, Amazon pushed for the USPS to install the mailbox there. This came after the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/amazon-union-vote-nlrb-mail-ballots-election-bessemer-alabama-2021-2\">NLRB rejected a bid from the company</a> to make in-person voting obligatory in February.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6059c6510d155e0019ef620a?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Mailbox Amazon Bessemer\" height=\"1000\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The mailbox outside the Amazon warehouse in Bessemer.\n<p class=\"copyright\">RWDSU</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>&#34;Even though the NLRB definitively denied Amazon&#39;s request for a drop box on the warehouse property, Amazon felt it was above the law and worked with the postal service anyway to install one. They did this because it provided a clear ability to intimidate workers,&#34; Appelbaum said in his statement.</p><p>&#34;We said from the beginning that we wanted all employees to vote and proposed many different options to try and make it easy,&#34; an Amazon spokesperson told Insider. &#34;The RWDSU fought those at every turn and pushed for a mail-only election, which the NLRB&#39;s own data showed would reduce turnout. This mailbox - which only the USPS had access to - was a simple, secure, and completely optional way to make it easy for employees to vote, no more and no less.&#34;</p><p>Amazon has been vocally anti-union, in some cases sending <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/amazon-union-alabama-workers-describe-anti-union-tactics-bessemer-2021-3\">multiple text messages a day to workers and handing out &#34;vote no&#34; pins.</a> The company has also repeatedly stated that its starting wage and benefits are comparable to what a union would offer.</p><p>The union effort received bipartisan support from politicians over the course of the vote. Sen. Bernie Sanders <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/bernie-sanders-visiting-amazon-workers-unionizing-alabama-2021-3\">visited Bessemer</a> along with union organizers to shore up support. Sen. Marco Rubio <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/rubio-brings-bipartisan-support-to-amazon-union-push-2021-3\">spoke out</a> in support of the union effort. And President Joe Biden <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/biden-defends-workers-rights-warns-of-threats-as-amazon-employees-vote-on-union-2021-3\">spoke broadly</a> about the benefits of unionization, but did not explicitly reference this union effort.</p><p>The union vote was marked by appeals from Amazon to change the NLRB&#39;s practices. In February, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/amazon-union-vote-nlrb-mail-ballots-election-bessemer-alabama-2021-2\">Insider reported</a> that the NLRB had denied Amazon&#39;s request to conduct an in-person union election, saying that the company must allow mail-in voting. And after the close of voting on March 29, the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/amazon-request-cameras-watch-union-vote-bessemer-ballot-boxes-rejected-2021-3\">NLRB denied a request</a> by Amazon for increased surveillance on the room where ballots were stored in the labor board&#39;s Birmingham, Alabama headquarters. </p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a and great-grandfather.&#34;</p><p>&#34;I wish to express my sincere condolences to Her Majesty Queen Elizabeth, The Royal Family and the British people upon the death of His Royal Highness The Prince border=\"0\"></img></a>\n</div><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/xDqDOX8ljzY\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Fri, 09 Apr 2021 15:55:27 +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/607071ea4943790018bb19de?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"6c06d0f68753cdd6693fa64672de1046","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn68@2020_5/2021/04/09/16-42-17-795_2f064dd1505c4f30.webp","destWidth":4200,"destHeight":3150,"sourceBytes":208932,"destBytes":208932,"author":"insider@insider.com (John Haltiwanger)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/607071db4943790018bb19dc?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn4@2020_2/2021/04/09/16-42-18-613_718a285907d62dc0.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn84@2020_2/2021/04/09/16-42-21-967_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=xDqDOX8ljzY:lFGTQiRuyRA:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn79@2020_1/2021/04/09/16-42-22-895_089f514dcb3303ac.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=xDqDOX8ljzY:lFGTQiRuyRA:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn64@2020_1/2021/04/09/16-42-21-940_0411b9d47251aa7c.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn91@2020_1/2021/04/09/16-42-19-669_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=xDqDOX8ljzY:lFGTQiRuyRA:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn83@2020_6/2021/04/09/16-42-18-398_0847a115e277c84c.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/xDqDOX8ljzY":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn27@2020_2/2021/04/09/16-42-18-947_5cd8fc35ea6018a3.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1617986505573},{"createdTime":"2021-04-10 00:41:45","updatedTime":"2021-04-10 00:41:45","title":"How a growing fight against a little-known ISIS affiliate pulled in US Green Berets and foreign mercenaries","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/fight-against-isis-affiliate-in-mozambique-draws-us-green-berets-2021-4","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6070782aa451820019b3a458?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Palma Pemba Cabo Delgado Mozambique\" height=\"1000\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Security officials stand guard as people wait for friends and relatives fleeing an attack claimed by ISIS-linked insurgents on Palma in Mozambique, April 1, 2021.\n<p class=\"copyright\">REUTERS/Emidio Jozine</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>US Army Green Berets are on the ground in Mozambique training the army to take on a growing insurgency linked to ISIS.</li>\n<li>Mozambique&#39;s inability to quell the violence has already drawn in Russian and South African mercenaries, who&#39;ve failed to counter the militants.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Last week, militants stormed the city of Palma in northeastern Mozambique&#39;s Cabo Delgado province.</p><p>The fighters attacked civilians with machetes and assault rifles, leaving behind beheaded and bullet-ridden bodies. Thousands of people have fled the besieged city for the coast.</p><p>The violence lasted several days and culminated at the Amarula Palma Hotel, an oasis for expats and foreign workers, where helicopters evacuated people barricaded inside and searched for others hiding nearby. Reports put the death toll anywhere from scores to hundreds.</p><p>The bloodshed was a surprise to most but likely not to the US Army Green Berets who have been in Cabo Delgado for weeks training Mozambique&#39;s army, according to a March report by <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2021/03/15/world/africa/mozambique-american-troops-isis-insurgency.html\">The New York Times</a>.</p><p>According to The Times, &#34;two dozen&#34; of the elite soldiers were in the region as part of an ongoing effort to contain the militant group Ansar al-Sunna, known locally as al-Shabbab (unrelated to the Somali jihadist group), which <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2021/03/30/world/africa/isis-mozambique-attack.html\">recently confirmed its affiliation with ISIS</a>.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60707666a451820019b3a44f?format=jpeg\" alt=\"C-130J soldier Maputo Mozambique\" height=\"1333\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A US soldier talks to a Mozambique soldier next to a US C-130J in Maputo, Mozambique, April 5, 2019.\n<p class=\"copyright\">US Air Force/Tech. Sgt. Chris Hibben</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>The soldiers were part of what the Special Forces refers to as a Joint Combined Exchange Training, or JCET. Special Operations Command Africa initiated the JCET in Mozambique in March, sending two Special Forces teams, each with 12 soldiers, to Cabo Delgado.</p><p>A source close to Army Special Forces told Insider that the JCET has been reinforced with a Crisis Response Force - the Special Forces equivalent of a Tier 1 counter-terrorism force.</p><p>According to the source, who spoke on the condition of anonymity, six 12-person Special Forces teams have been deployed to Mozambique.</p><p>Special Operations Command Africa, however, denied any CRF had deployed.</p><p>&#34;There are no Contingency Response Forces from 3rd [Special Forces Group] or any other US unit in Mozambique,&#34; a spokesperson said. &#34;The team currently in Mozambique is only there to conduct a Joint Combined Exchange Training.&#34;</p><h2>Militants, mercenaries, and civilians under fire</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/607074444943790018bb19f3?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Car ambush Palma Mozambique\" height=\"728\" width=\"970\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A wrecked car involved in an ambush on civilians fleeing Palma, seen between March 24 and March 27, 2021.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Dyck Advisory Group/Handout via REUTERS</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Carried out all over the world, JCETs are billed as a way for Special Forces soldiers to get first-hand experience with foreign militaries, learn mission-essential skills, and build their local knowledge.</p><p>JCETs also allow the US military to put eyes on the ground in regions where conflict may be brewing, but they have been criticized for inadvertently equipping foreign forces with skills that are misused when the US departs.</p><p>On March 10, the US State Department <a href=\"https://www.state.gov/state-department-terrorist-designations-of-isis-affiliates-and-leaders-in-the-democratic-republic-of-the-congo-and-mozambique/\">designated</a> Ansar al-Sunna as a terrorist organization and officially confirmed its ties to ISIS. Conservative estimates put the current al-Sunna fighting force at 800 insurgents and growing rapidly.</p><p>The designation is not unfounded, based <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2021/03/28/world/africa/mozambique-palma-hotel-insurgents.html\">on the violence</a> attributed to <a href=\"https://www.amnesty.org/en/latest/news/2021/03/mozambique-civilians-killed-as-war-crimes-committed-by-armed-group-government-forces-and-private-military-contractors-new-report/\">the group&#39;s fighters</a> in recent years. But it has become common for the US to issue such designations prior to clandestine operations against those organizations.</p><p>Such designations allow special-operations forces to receive air support and, more importantly, <a href=\"https://www.jstor.org/stable/resrep11764\">US Predator drones</a>. US laws allow authorization for strikes to be made by US commanders on the ground when US forces are conducting counter-terrorism operations.</p><p>Mozambique&#39;s government has attempted to subdue al-Sunna, and many have criticized the government for <a href=\"https://www.greydynamics.com/blood-fields-mozambique-insurgency-and-isis-resurgence/?highlight=Mozambique\">draconian measures and heavy-handed military operations</a> that do little to distinguish civilians from insurgents and only exacerbate the humanitarian crisis.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6070780d4943790018bb1a10?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Pemba Cabo Delgado Mozambique soldiers\" height=\"1333\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Mozambican soldiers at the airport in Pemba, the capital of Cabo Delgado, March 31, 2021.\n<p class=\"copyright\">AFP via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Unable to quell the violence, the government first turned to the Wanger Group, a Russian security firm linked to the Kremlin. The group is owned by Yevgeny Preghozin, a Russian oligarch who is very close to Putin, and its fighters are deployed across Africa and the Middle East, often acting in alignment with Moscow&#39;s interests.</p><p>In 2019, Wagner mobilized a large force, including helicopter gunships, against al-Sunna in Cabo Delgado. The militant group was supported by ISIS and with fighters and equipment from neighboring nations. Wagner&#39;s forces were foiled, in large part by a lack of experience in the region, and <a href=\"https://sofrep.com/news/wagner-group-russian-mercenaries-still-foundering-in-africa/\">quickly retreated to Nacala</a>, roughly 250 miles to the south.</p><p>The Mozambique government then turned to the Dyke Advisory Group, or DAG, a South African private military contractor.</p><p>DAG encountered the same problems: a growing insurgency supported by international terror organizations and enmeshed with the local population. The <a href=\"https://www.amnesty.org/en/latest/news/2021/03/mozambique-civilians-killed-as-war-crimes-committed-by-armed-group-government-forces-and-private-military-contractors-new-report/\">Amnesty International report</a> also attributes atrocities to DAG, citing eyewitness accounts of DAG operatives firing from helicopters &#34;indiscriminately into crowds of people&#34; as well as repeatedly firing on civilian infrastructure, like hospitals and homes.</p><p>DAG had little success against al-Sunna. When the insurgents stormed Palma, the helicopters DAG used for assault operations became rescue birds. DAG helos reportedly <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2021/03/28/world/africa/mozambique-palma-hotel-insurgents.html\">helped evacuate 200 civilians</a> from the cut-off Aramula Palma Hotel.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6070740ba451820019b3a437?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Palma Mozambique Dyck Advisory Group helicopter\" height=\"1200\" width=\"1600\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A Dyck Advisory Group helicopter lands in Palma, Mozambique, sometime between March 24 and March 27, 2021.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Dyck Advisory Group/Handout via REUTERS</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>The recent violence comes at a crucial moment for DAG, whose relationship with the Mozambique government has frayed.</p><p>DAG personnel have spent months training Mozambique&#39;s military with helicopters the group <a href=\"https://www.defenceweb.co.za/aerospace/military-helicopters/gazelles-delivered-to-mozambican-air-force/\">imported</a> from Britain to supplement the military&#39;s own helicopters, which are variants of the Mi-24 attack helicopter.</p><p>But DAG has struggled with this assignment in Cabo Delgado. Several reports of downed aircraft have leaked out of the wartorn province over the past year, including one that <a href=\"https://www.defenceweb.co.za/aerospace/military-helicopters/gazelle-crash-in-mozambique-confirmed/\">militants carrying the now trademark ISIS flag</a> celebrated in a video released by ISIS&#39;s media wing.</p><p>DAG&#39;s owner, Lionel Dyke, has bristled about the difficulties the group has faced.</p><p>&#34;We are doing something that nobody else can do or has wanted to do, so use what you have got. And if it is not efficient, fire us. It&#39;s as simple as that,&#34; <a href=\"https://www.cnn.com/2021/03/30/africa/lionel-dyck-mozambique-insurgents-hold-palma-intl/index.html\">he told CNN</a> on March 31.</p><p>Mozambique&#39;s government <a href=\"https://www.irishtimes.com/news/world/africa/mozambique-government-terminates-south-african-military-company-s-contract-1.4526386\">terminated the contract</a> the next day.</p><h2>Scramble for Cabo Delgado&#39;s resources</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6070740aa451820019b3a436?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Afungi liquified natural gas Mozambique\" height=\"533\" width=\"800\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The Afungi Liquified Natural Gas Camp in Afungi, Mozambique.\n<p class=\"copyright\">WFP/Handout via REUTERS</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>The backdrop to the violence and efforts to quell it is Cabo Delgado&#39;s valuable natural resources, which Mozambique&#39;s government is using to lure foreign support.</p><p>Cabo Delgado is home to one of Africa&#39;s largest natural gas reserves. Discovered in 2010, the gas was initially a source of hope for the people of Cabo Delgado. Locals believed the reserves would lead to good jobs and boost the beleaguered local economy.</p><p>But Mozambique&#39;s central government - particularly its ruling party - dealt with gas companies directly <a href=\"https://www.bbc.com/news/world-africa-54183948\">in exchange for most of the profits</a>. Locals, mostly struggling subsistence farmers and fishermen, were left out, with many losing access to their farmland and fisheries.</p><p>People in Cabo Delgado, a majority-Muslim province, were already frustrated by long-standing <a href=\"https://www.bbc.com/news/world-africa-54183948\">government corruption</a> as well as <a href=\"https://www.bbc.com/news/world-africa-52532741\">isolation and discrimination</a> from the rest of the country. As it has elsewhere, ISIS capitalized on local anger to expand its operations, spreading its message of radicalization.</p><p>Islamists from elsewhere in Africa set up mosques in Cabo Delgado and promoted rumors that local imams were allied with the corrupt government, <a href=\"https://www.bbc.com/news/world-africa-54183948\">Mozambique expert Joseph Hanlon wrote in a report for the BBC</a>. These Islamists began providing financial assistance to local communities and told residents their lives would be better under stringent Islamic law, known as Sharia.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/607078c64943790018bb1a17?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Cabo Delgado Mozambique displaced persons\" height=\"1333\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>People who fled attacks by insurgents in the northern part of Cabo Delgado at a meeting in Matuge in northern Mozambique, February 24, 2021.\n<p class=\"copyright\">ALFREDO ZUNIGA/AFP via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>To receive support from ISIS - mostly in the form of weapons - all the locals, and later the members of Ansar al-Sunna, had to do was recognize ISIS, promoting the group&#39;s propaganda and efforts to expand.</p><p>For its efforts, ISIS can extend its reach to a new region - where ungoverned spaces further facilitate that expansion - and access valuable resources, profits from which can be <a href=\"https://www.rand.org/blog/2018/10/the-power-of-affiliates-which-islamic-state-franchise.html\">redistributed to other needy franchises</a>.</p><p>That violence and the stakes involved are why US Special Operations Command has tripled its forces in the province.</p><p>The response likely reflects a mix of political and commercial interests. Washington may see continued chaos in Cabo Delgado as a threat that will surely benefit ISIS and its operations in Africa. US firms may also be looking to secure <a href=\"https://www.theafricareport.com/34573/despite-oil-gloom-total-rallies-14bn-for-mozambique-project/\">access to the precious natural gas</a> that foreign companies are already jockeying to exploit.</p><p>Mozambique is now on the list of African nations where the US is deeply involved. The fighting in Cabo Delgado is far from over, but what remains uncertain is whether the elite Green Berets and deadly drones they wield will be stymied like the Russians and South Africans before them.</p><p><em>J.W. Sotak is a defense and foreign-policy reporter who focuses on the Middle East and Africa. He is a 10-year veteran of the US Army and served as part of a Army Civil Affairs Provincial Reconstruction Team in Afghanistan. His reports have been published on SOFREP and the New York Times. You can follow him on Twitter at @JWSotak.</em></p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a n48@2020_4/2021/04/09/16-42-19-854_790524d3151a243c.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/xlywLDgfS2g":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn48@2020_5/2021/04/09/16-42-17-862_4725abc231d1d4ed.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1617986505537},{"createdTime":"2021-04-10 speaks at the World Food Program USA&#39;s Annual McGovern-Dole Leadership Award Ceremony at Organization of American States on April 12, 2016 in Washington, DC.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.gettyimages.com/detail/news-photo/world-food-program-usa-board-chairman-hunter-biden-speaks-news-photo/520762182?adppopup=true\" target=\"_blank\">Paul Morigi/Getty Images for World Food Program USA</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>The Daily Mail claims to have verified Hunter Biden&#39;s laptop, and published explicit images from it. </li>\n<li>The computer left in a Delaware repair shop, and was the subject of intense controversy last year. </li>\n<li>The outlet argued that it shows a side of Biden he wasn&#39;t transparent about in his new book.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p><a href=\"https://www.dailymail.co.uk/news/article-9445105/What-Hunter-Biden-left-tell-memoir-revealed.html\">The Daily Mail claims that</a> forensics experts have verified the authenticity of messages and images in a laptop containing lurid details of Hunter Biden&#39;s private life.</p><p>DailyMail.com, the US-focused website run by the British tabloid, published a long article detailing the laptop&#39;s contents on Thursday.</p><p>The laptop was the subject of intense controversy in the runup to the November presidential election, when <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/new-york-post-hunter-joe-biden-giuliani-red-flags-disinformation-2020-10\">The New York Post claimed</a> that the laptop contained emails harmful to Joe Biden.</p><p>The Post claimed Biden - then the Democratic nominee for president - was compromised by his son&#39;s business dealings in Ukraine, where he worked on the board of energy firm Burisma. </p><p>Other emails, said critics, contained evidence of influence-peddling by Hunter Biden in China. Neither claim was ever substantiated.</p><p>The story of how the Post and later the Mail obtained the machine is convoluted, with it having initially reportedly been abandoned in a Delaware computer shop then handed to allies of Donald Trump. </p><p>Amid doubts over the authenticity of the information, and briefings from US intelligence agencies that it was likely <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/biden-laptop-real-fake-russian-intelligence-2020-10\">part of a Russian disinformation campaign,</a> Facebook and Twitter introduced measures to stop it being shared. </p><p>But according to the Mail, the laptop is indeed Hunter Biden&#39;s, and contains 103,000 text messages, 154,000 emails, and more than 2,000 photos.</p><p>The Mail said the contents were verified by cyber forensics experts at Maryman &#38; Associates, a California-based company which <a href=\"http://www.maryman.com/our-firm/\">says on its website</a> has 20 years of experience.</p><p>The company claims to have matched contents of the laptop with email addresses, contents from an iPad, and an iPhone serial number connected to Biden.</p><p>Insider attempted to reach Hunter Biden for comment with emails to his attorney and book publishers, but did not immediately receive a response.</p><p>The publication of new material from the laptop comes days after the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/hunter-bidens-memoir-beautiful-things-out-in-april-2021-2\">publication of Hunter Biden&#39;s memoir,</a> &#34;Beautiful Things,&#34; where he describes his struggles with drug addiction. </p><p>The Mail claims the material from the laptop shows that Hunter Biden &#34;chose not to divulge&#34; parts of his life in the book.  </p><p>It published pictures of Hunter Biden which it said showed him with prostitutes, and showed evidence of drug use.</p><p>There is no politically substantive new information in the report. It claims to contain text messages between Biden and his father, most of which show the elder Biden offering Hunter support.</p><p>The Mail claims material from the computer show that Hunter Biden was able to evade prosecution for drugs and prostitution offences.</p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">-Aaron Rupar  (@atrupar) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1380379731753893890?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">April 9, 2021</a></blockquote><script async=\"\" src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script><p>It contains details of messages from Hunter Biden about an incident in which the Secret Service got involved after he abandoned a firearm in a bin after an argument with Hallie Biden, the wife of his deceased brother Beau Biden, with whom he was having a relationship. The Secret Service denied any involvement in the incident. </p><p>The images were seized upon by Fox News hosts on Thursday night, who renewed their attacks on Hunter Biden and showed explicit stills from videos reportedly found on the laptop. </p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">-Curtis Houck  (@CurtisHouck) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1380382089921585153?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">April 9, 2021</a></blockquote><script async=\"\" src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script><p>Hunter Biden is currently <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/hunter-biden-tax-investigation-subpoena-asks-for-burisma-information-2020-12\">under investigation by federal authorities</a> regarding possible tax crimes relating to his work in Ukraine and China. </p><p>In an appearance on &#34;Jimmy Kimmel Live!&#34; Thursday to promote his book, Hunter Biden addressed some of the controversies, including the laptop. He has previously claimed that he doesn&#39;t know if the device was his.</p><p>He said: &#34;Now look, I really don&#39;t know and the fact of the matter is, it&#39;s a red herring. It is absolutely a red herring. But I am absolutely, I think, within my rights to question anything that comes from the desk of Rudy Giuliani. And so I don&#39;t know is the answer.&#34;</p><p>Giuliani has said that he played a part in getting the laptop to members of the media.</p><p>Last year Trump allies seized on an email in the laptop which appeared to show Hunter trying to broker a meeting between an associate at Burisma and Joe Biden while he was Barack Obama&#39;s Vice President. No evidence has emerged to indicate the meeting ever took place.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.politico.com/news/2020/10/14/biden-campaign-lashes-out-new-york-post-429486\">In a statement to Politico last year a Biden spokesman</a> said Joe Biden may have had an &#34;informal interaction&#34; with the Burisma associate of his son&#39;s but any interaction would&#39;ve been &#34;cursory.&#34; </p><p>After being abandoned in the computer repair shop, the laptop hard drive is s<a href=\"https://www.politico.com/news/2020/10/22/hunter-biden-giuliani-hard-drive-431022\">aid to have been obtained by Rudy Giuliani</a>, then working as Donald Trump&#39;s personal lawyer.</p><p>Giuliani led a longstanding campaign to link Joe Biden to his son&#39;s dealings in Ukraine. Former Trump advisor Steve Bannon was also said to be involved in handling the hard drive. It was then handed to the Post. </p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a Sakuma</p> \n  </figcaption> </img>\n</figure>\n<ul class=\"summary-list\"> \n <li>McDonald's will close all but 150 locations inside Walmart stores by this summer.</li> \n <li>The closures have been planned for over a year.</li> \n <li>Walmart is opening Domino's and other businesses in those leased space.</li> \n <li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider's business page</a>.</li> \n</ul>\n<p>McDonald's will continue the planned closing of hundreds of restaurants inside Walmart stores, <a href=\"https://www.wsj.com/articles/mcdonalds-is-closing-hundreds-of-its-walmart-restaurants-11617960602\">The Wall Street Journal reported.</a></p>\n<p>Walmart leases space, often near the front of its stores, to other businesses, usually restaurants. The big box chain partners with national chains and local businesses, depending on the needs of the community, a spokesperson told Insider. Pizza chain Domino's is an especially good fit, since the restaurants mostly depend on pick-up and delivery, they said.</p>\n<p>So far there are <a href=\"https://www.wsj.com/articles/mcdonalds-is-closing-hundreds-of-its-walmart-restaurants-11617960602\">30 Domino's in Walmarts</a> across the country, WSJ reported, noting that Walmart is also working with Taco Bell on installing locations.</p>\n<p><em><strong>Read more: </strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/retailers-physical-locaiton-outlook-predictions-post-pandemic-2021-4\" data-e2e-name=\"inline-read-more-link\">Experts say brick-and-mortar retailers could rebound post-pandemic - but only if they channel the e-commerce boom back to their physical outposts</a></em></p>\n<p>Not all leased Walmart storefronts are restaurants, and they're often tailored to specific needs of the area. For example, a store in rural Texas has a tool rental shop that wouldn't necessarily make sense in other areas, Walmart says. </p>\n<p>Walmart and McDonald's have worked together since 1994, with 800 locations in 2012 and about 500 in 2012.</p>\n<p>Two series of closures were planned for 2020 before the COVID-19 pandemic, with another wave planned to finish this summer, leaving 150 remaining locations. McDonald's has previously shared these plans with shareholders in earnings calls, including saying \"the majority of closures across the U.S. market are from <a href=\"https://corporate.mcdonalds.com/content/dam/gwscorp/assets/investors/financial-information/2021%20Planned%20Net%20Unit%20Openings%20by%20Segment.pdf\">lower sales volume</a> McDonald's in Walmart store locations,\" in a fourth quarter 2020 note on openings and closings.</p>\n<p>The business relationship between Walmart and McDonald's no longer made sense for either business. McDonald's restaurants inside Walmarts don't have drive-thrus, which have become increasingly important across the fast food industry. <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/starbucks-chick-fil-a-drive-thrus-ipads-and-video-technology-2021-3\">70% of orders</a> in top markets come from drive-thrus, the chain says.</p>\n<p>Meanwhile, Walmart has been growing e-commerce and curbside pickup, meaning that fewer customers were coming inside and deciding to buy McDonald's during the trip. COVID-19 also accelerated this trend as indoor dining was closed in many locations.</p>\n<p>\"We have a great opportunity with our leased space business to help our stores become even more convenient and relevant to local communities. We are excited to continue to bring in new businesses that make sense for our customers and their changing needs,\" Walmart told Insider. </p>\n<p>Some of Walmart's competitors rely on in-store restaurants. Some Target stores have <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/reviews/out?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.target.com%2Fc%2Fstarbucks%2F-%2FN-5cofw%3FNao%3D0\">Starbucks</a> locations inside, and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/costco-reopening-food-courts-adding-back-menu-items-2021-4\">Costco</a> is reopening its fan-favorite food courts.</p>\n<p><em>Do you have a story to share about a retail or restaurant chain? 00:41:45","updatedTime":"2021-04-10 00:41:45","title":"Prince Philip once lit up enemy ships as Royal Navy warships tore them apart during a bloody nighttime WWII naval battle","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/prince-philip-helped-sink-enemy-ships-during-world-war-ii-2021-4","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/607067edf068cf0018022be4?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Lieutenant Philip Mountbatten, then the husband of Princess Elizabeth, resumes his attendance at the Royal Naval Officers&#39; School at Kingsmoor in Hawthorn, Wiltshire on July 31, 1947\" height=\"424\" width=\"848\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Lieutenant Philip Mountbatten, then the husband of Princess Elizabeth, resumes his attendance at the Royal Naval Officers&#39; School at Kingsmoor in Hawthorn, Wiltshire on July 31, 1947\n<p class=\"copyright\">PNA Rota/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Prince Philip, who died Friday at the age of 99, was a decorated WWII combat veteran.</li>\n<li>He earned a valor award for lighting up enemy ships in a nighttime battle, helping the British achieve victory.</li>\n<li>He is also credited with helping save his ship from an enemy bomber in a battle two years later.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Prince Philip, <a href=\"https://www.insider.com/prince-philip-dead-2021-3\">who died on Friday at the age of 99</a>, was a decorated World War II veteran who fought in a number of naval battles, including one bloody exchange in the dead of night.</p><p>Allied forces delivered a devastating blow to the Italian navy at Cape Matapan just off Greece on March 28, 1941, sinking several enemy vessels.</p><p>Three British Royal Navy battleships closed with Italian warships in the dark, catching the enemy force off guard. It was the kind of close-quarters gun battle that ship radar advancements would make rare. Philip, who was then a 19-year-old midshipman on the HMS Valiant, was manning the searchlights for finding enemies that night.</p><p>&#34;I seem to remember that I reported that I had a target in sight, and was ordered to &#39;open shutter&#39;. The beam lit up a stationary cruiser, but we were so close by then that the beam only lit up half the ship,&#34; <a href=\"https://www.thedailybeast.com/philip-how-i-sunk-italian-cruisers\">Philip recalled in the forward of the 2012 history book <em>Dark Seas: The Battle of Cape Matapan</em></a>.</p><p>Philip said that &#34;at this point all hell broke loose as all our eight 15-inch guns started firing at the stationary cruiser, which disappeared in an explosion and a cloud of smoke.&#34;</p><p>&#34;I was then ordered to &#39;train left&#39; and lit up another Italian cruiser, which was given the same treatment,&#34; he said.</p><p>During the nighttime fight, British warships sank three cruisers and two destroyers, some in a matter of minutes. The Italians lost more than 2,000 sailors. <a href=\"https://www.history.co.uk/article/prince-philip-and-the-invasion-of-sicily\">One account from the battle said</a> that &#34;thousands of bodies were strung over fifteen miles of sea off Cape Matapan.&#34;</p><p>For his actions during the battle, Philip was awarded the Greek War Cross, a military decoration for heroism.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60706834a451820019b3a3a5?format=jpeg\" alt=\"British Royal Navy Battleship HMS Valiant\" height=\"641\" width=\"1024\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>British Royal Navy Battleship HMS Valiant\n<p class=\"copyright\">Arkivi/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Two years later, Philip took part in the allied invasion of Sicily, serving as a first lieutenant and second-in-command aboard the destroyer HMS Wallace, a ship he is credited with helping save from an enemy bomber with a bit of quick thinking.</p><p>Harry Hargreaves, a former Royal Navy sailor who served with Philip aboard the Wallace, <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/uk/2003/dec/28/monarchy.davidsmith\">recalled the events of the 1943 fight in the early 2000s</a> in discussions with British media.</p><p>He said that the Wallace was facing almost certain destruction by a German Luftwaffe bomber. &#34;It was obvious that we were the target for tonight and they would not stop until we had suffered a fatal hit,&#34; he said.</p><p>He said that in that terrifying moment, he saw Philip in a hurried conversation with the ship&#39;s captain, presumably trying to come up with a plan of action before the bomber came back around.</p><p>&#34;The next thing a wooden raft was being put together on deck,&#34; the former yeoman said. &#34;Within five minutes they launched the raft over the side, at each end was fastened a smoke float.&#34; Once the raft was in the water, smoke began to billow up, as it might from a wounded warship.</p><p>The captain relocated the Wallace and then ordered engines stopped, sitting quietly in the darkness, bracing for the next attack. When the bomber circled back around for another run, it targeted the raft billowing smoke as though on fire. The plan had worked.</p><p>&#34;Prince Philip saved our lives that night,&#34; <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/uk/2003/dec/28/monarchy.davidsmith\">Hargreaves told British media</a>. &#34;He was always very courageous and resourceful and thought very quickly. You would say to yourself &#39;What the hell are we going to do now?&#39; and Philip would come up with something.&#34;</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6070692da451820019b3a3ad?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Queen Elizabeth II wearing the Imperial State Crown and the Duke of Edinburgh in uniform of Admiral of the Fleet wave from the balcony to the onlooking crowds around the gates of Buckingham Palace after the Coronation\" height=\"716\" width=\"1024\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Queen Elizabeth II wearing the Imperial State Crown and the Duke of Edinburgh in uniform of Admiral of the Fleet wave from the balcony to the onlooking crowds around the gates of Buckingham Palace after the Coronation\n<p class=\"copyright\">PA Images via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Several years after the end of World War II, Philip became admiral of the Sea Cadet Corps, colonel-in-chief of the Army Cadet Force, and air commodore-in-chief of the Air Training Corps. The following year, he was promoted to admiral of the fleet, field marshal, and marshal of the Royal Air Force.</p><p>Philip met his future wife of more than seven decades, Queen Elizabeth II, as a young cadet at the Britannia Royal Naval College in Dartmouth just a few years before the war.</p><p>&#34;It is with deep sorrow that Her Majesty The Queen has announced the death of her beloved husband, His Royal Highness The Prince Philip, Duke of Edinburgh,&#34; <a href=\"https://twitter.com/RoyalFamily/status/1380475865323212800\">Buckingham Palace announced Friday</a>. &#34;His Royal Highness passed away peacefully this morning at Windsor Castle.&#34;</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a It breaks down how he wants to govern.","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/bidens-budget-priorities-congress-democrats-next-year-to-go-2021-4","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/604fa9bffe6a340019acec25?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Biden stimulus\" height=\"1000\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>President Joe Biden speaks about the COVID-19 relief package in the State Dining Room of the White House, Monday, March 15, 2021, in Washington.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Patrick Semansky/AP</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Biden unveiled an early budget proposal on Friday that would ramp up spending on education and public housing.</li>\n<li>Military spending would not change under Biden&#39;s $1.5 trillion proposal, which Congress must approve.</li>\n<li data-stringify-indent=\"0\">It proposes a $118 billion, or 16%, increase in domestic spending from Trump&#39;s last budget.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>The White House <a href=\"https://www.whitehouse.gov/omb/fy-2022-discretionary-request/\">unveiled its initial $1.5 trillion budget proposal</a> on Friday. The plan represents a an early glimpse into President Joe Biden&#39;s domestic spending priorities, ramping up spending on education, health, and climate initiatives while keeping military spending relatively flat.</p><p>It&#39;s Biden&#39;s first budgetary pitch to Congress, which can also reshape it in an aproppriations process which will likely take months.</p><p>The so-called &#34;skinny budget&#34; calls for an $118 billion increase in discretionary spending from fiscal year 2021 - the type of spending that lawmakers can change from one year to the next. That would be a 16% increase from current levels of domestic spending. Programs like Social Security and Medicare are not included, and will be part of a fuller spending proposal later in the spring.</p><p>The 58-page Biden blueprint includes significant spending boosts to agencies critical to achieving his domestic priorities, such as the Education Department.  Other increases include:</p><ul><li>Department of Education (+41% from last year).</li><li>Department of Commerce (+28%).</li><li>Department of Health and Human Services (+23%).</li><li>Environmental Protection Agency (+21%).</li><li>National Science Foundation (+20%).</li><li>Department of Defense, relatively unchanged from existing levels.</li></ul><p>The pot of money also includes $69 billion to expand public housing. It also proposes a new medical research agency with the aim of curing diseases like cancer, <a href=\"https://www.statnews.com/2021/04/09/white-house-push-new-agency-aimed-at-curing-cancer/\">Stat News reported.</a></p><p>In a letter to congressional leaders, acting Office Management and Budget Director Shalanda Young said the current crisis brings with it &#34;a moment of possibility.&#34;</p><p>&#34;The upcoming appropriations process is another important opportunity to continue laying a stronger foundation for the future and reversing a legacy of chronic disinvestment in crucial priorities,&#34; she wrote.</p><p>This is a sharp break from President Donald Trump&#39;s conservative agenda. Trump&#39;s <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/budget-proposal-trump-whats-included-main-points-safety-net-2021-2020-2-1028893397#military1\">budget plan last year</a> sought to slash major domestic programs such as Medicaid and the size of federal agencies including the Environmental Protection Agency.</p><p>This budget arrives as the White House prepares to dive into congressional negotiations on its multitrillion-dollar infrastructure package, with Congress returning to session next week. Lawmakers must also strike a deal on the federal budget before funding expires at the end of September.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-bidens-2-trillion-infrastructure-plan-means-for-you-2021-4\">Biden&#39;s $2.3 trillion infrastructure package</a> would allocate major funding to roads and bridges, clean energy incentives, and in-home elder care, among other measures. A second proposal of a similar size is expected later this month. These plans are separate from the White House budget plan.</p><p>House Speaker Nancy Pelosi said on Thursday that Democrats could opt to bypass Republicans to approve the package sometime in July. The GOP is strongly opposed to the scope of the plan as well as its corporate tax hikes.</p><p>&#34;If we have to go to reconciliation, that&#39;s a lever, but I hope it&#39;s not something that we need to do,&#34; Pelosi said.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a 00:41:45","updatedTime":"2021-04-10 00:41:45","title":"Credit Suisse reins in hedge fund limits following $4.7 billion loss tied to Archegos Capital, report says","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/credit-suisse-hedge-fund-limits-billions-loss-archegos-capital-hwang-2021-4","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60706fefa451820019b3a408?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Credit Suisse\" height=\"1249\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Arnd Wiegmann/Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul><li><strong>Credit Suisse is reining in limits on hedge funds following the $20 billion Archegos Capital meltdown, <a href=\"https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2021-04-08/credit-suisse-tightens-hedge-fund-limits-amid-archegos-fallout\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">according to a Bloomberg report</a>.</strong></li><li><strong>The financial giant will absorb a $4.7 billion writedown after Bill Hwang&#39;s family office was forced to liquidate its entire portfolio, to which the bank was heavily exposed.</strong></li><li><strong>Credit Suisse is now shifting to a dynamic margin requirement for clients that utilize swap agreements, according to Bloomberg.</strong></li><li><a href=\"https://newsletter.businessinsider.com/join/4np/10-things-opening-bell?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingesttm_medium=ingest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong>Sign up here for our daily newsletter, 10 Things Before the Opening Bell</strong></a><strong>.</strong></li></ul><hr><p>Credit Suisse is implementing new limits on hedge fund clients that utilize swap agreements following <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/bill-hwang-lost-20-billion-2-days-archegos-collapse-report-2021-4-1030288757\">the $20 billion meltdown of Archegos Capital</a>.</p><p>Bill Hwang&#39;s family office, Archegos, utilized equity-swap agreements to take on massive leverage and <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/archegos-capital-margin-call-20-billion-liquidation-8-stocks-plummeted-2021-3-1030254795\">make concentrated bets on a handful of stocks</a> like ViacomCBS and Discovery.</p><p>But a sharp decline in ViacomCBS sparked a massive margin call that Archegos was unable to meet, leading to a massive liquidation that cost some banks billions of dollars in losses. Credit Suisse seems to have been most exposed to Archegos after not unwinding Hwang&#39;s positions fast enough amid the market tumult last month. The bank said it <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/credit-suisse-posts-loss-after-archegos-blow-up-exec-departure-2021-4-1030275805\">booked a $4.7 billion writedown related to the event</a>.</p><p>Now, to prevent a similar blowup from happening again, Credit Suisse is tightening its financing terms given to hedge funds and family offices, according to <a href=\"https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2021-04-08/credit-suisse-tightens-hedge-fund-limits-amid-archegos-fallout\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a Bloomberg report.</a></p><p>The bank is changing its margin requirement on swap agreements to dynamic from static, which is similar to the terms given in its prime-brokerage contracts, Bloomberg said, citing people with direct knowledge of the matter. A dynamic margin requirement would force its clients to post more collateral as a position moves down, rather than setting a fixed margin requirement at the onset of the contract.</p><p>The shift to dynamic margin requirements will increase the costs for hedge funds and family offices looking to unitize swap agreements, making the trades less profitable. Credit Suisse is now asking some clients to immediately switch to the news margin methodology, according to the report. </p><p>Whether Credit Suisse&#39;s move is more indicative of a broader limitation on the leverage hedge funds and family offices can take on remains to be seen.</p><p>It would not be surprising if some banks follow suit, given that the Switzerland-based bank wasn&#39;t the only one that lost billions. <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/nomura-takes-2-billion-loss-after-last-weeks-sell-off-2021-3-1030252569\">Nomura has said it lost as much as $2 billion related to the Archegos liquidation,</a> and JPMorgan has estimated that the collective losses of multiple banks could reach $10 billion.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/crypto-arbitrage-trading-strategy-alameda-research-sam-bankman-fried-billionaire-2021-4\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">A 29-year-old self-made billionaire Terms of the deal were not disclosed. </p><p>FuboTV has become one of the go-to streaming providers for consumers looking to add a sports package to their streaming lineup after cutting the cable TV
